From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr  1 00:58:58 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Norman Makoto Su)
Date: Mon, 1 Apr 2002 08:58:58 +0900
Subject: [Xitami] LRWP
References: <200203291500.DAA24626@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <007501c1d910$05c5fc90$dd31200a@JAZZ>

Hi, thanks for the reply.

> One request per connection, at a time.  If you need to handle multiple
> requests at once just open multiple connections.  If there is more than
> one LRWP of the same "name" connected, then they'll be given the
> requests in either round-robin or first-free fashion (depending on the
> configuration option).

So, in anycase, there is no way for one LRWP to know about the other LRWP
connections (w/o some kind of explicit messaging via files/sockets/etc between
the LRWP programs)?

Thanks,

Norman Su


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr  1 02:06:48 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 01 Apr 2002 13:06:48 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] LRWP
In-Reply-To: Message from "Norman Makoto Su" <normsu@slab.tnr.sharp.co.jp>
 of "Mon, 01 Apr 2002 08:58:58 +0900." <007501c1d910$05c5fc90$dd31200a@JAZZ>
Message-ID: <200204010106.NAA23375@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <007501c1d910$05c5fc90$dd31200a@JAZZ>, "Norman Makoto Su" writes:
>> One request per connection, at a time.  If you need to handle multiple
>> requests at once just open multiple connections.  If there is more than
>> one LRWP of the same "name" connected, then they'll be given the
>> requests in either round-robin or first-free fashion (depending on the
>> configuration option).
>
>So, in anycase, there is no way for one LRWP to know about the other LRWP
>connections (w/o some kind of explicit messaging via files/sockets/etc between
>the LRWP programs)?

Yup.  But if it's all in one process (eg, using threads, or SMT) then
the LRWP connections will "know about each other" anyway.  The Java
Servlet Runner uses this sort of approach to handle state between the
servlets.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr  1 02:54:00 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 01 Apr 2002 13:54:00 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] LRWP
In-Reply-To: Message from "Norman Makoto Su" <normsu@slab.tnr.sharp.co.jp>
 of "Mon, 01 Apr 2002 10:21:17 +0900." <011c01c1d91b$85c96fc0$dd31200a@JAZZ>
Message-ID: <200204010154.NAA23535@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <011c01c1d91b$85c96fc0$dd31200a@JAZZ>, "Norman Makoto Su" writes:
>Would you mind explaining what you mean by "just open multiple connections"?
>I'm not sure why its all in one process-- don't you have to run multiple LRWP
>peers (each which have their own memory space, etc)?  I think I'm
>misunderstanding something.

The original question was whether a LRWP peer could handle multiple
requests simultaneously (ie, overlapping), to which my response was
"just open multiple connections" (there is only one request at a time per
connection).

You can achieve the multiple connections by running multiple instances
of the LRWP peer (ie, multiple processes), and that'll work fine.  But
if the LRWP instances need to share data then they'll have to do it via
a database (common technique), or via shared memory, a private
connection, etc.

If you want to avoid the overhead of reading/writing to a database, and
the hassle of shared memory code (particularly portable shared memory
code), then you could simply write a LRWP peer that opens multiple
sockets connected to Xitami, and registers itself on each one.  As far
as Xitami is concerned it's multiple LRWP peers, and they'll be used in
a round-robin fashion (or in a first-available fashion; depending on how
Xitami is configured).

There are basically three ways to handle the "multiple
connections/requests in one process" situation:
- OS level threading (kernel or system library threading)
- select()-style loops
- SMT

While you can do select()-style loops by hand, the design will rapidly
drive you nuts if it is of any size.  SMT allows you to abstract the
design further, and gives you "thread-like" execution of the
select()-style loop handling.

The important thing to remember is that as far as Xitami is concerned,
LRWP peers are just a socket connection to it, that has registered.  It
doesn't know anything else about them, and it doesn't care.  It just
sends them requests to be handled across the socket, one request per
socket.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr  1 17:34:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 1 Apr 2002 11:34:21 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Questions configuring Xitami
In-Reply-To: <3CA5D6B7.30198.163F21E@localhost>
References: <3CA5D6B7.30198.163F21E@localhost>
Message-ID: <127357039495.20020401113421@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Won't the broadband connections take the lion share of the
> bandwidth (being able to take more faster in shorter time frame)
> leaving the dialups with the scraps of what they can down feed in
> a bandwidth crunch?

The effect is insignificant. The chunks are small and Xitami serves
data very soon after each packet is requested. The 56K connections
tend to get about all the data they can handle.

> My experience with running Xitami under NT 4 was it would run fine
> for a week to a month then Xitami would suddenly stop taking
> connections.

Which Xitami? Under NT, the Service Version is most stable.

The TCP/IP stack in NT 4 is flawed (not as flawed as in Win31, which
would stall every few days). However, my NT4 server runs for months
at a time, has been up since September. What seems to stall it (or
NT's IP stack) is certain FTP clients that my helpers use for huge
site uploads.

One thing- Xitami on NT4 "appears" more stable on my P-350/128M box
than it did on my P-150/32M box. While neither Xitami nor the TCP
stack needs much memory, and indeed it tended to sit with 24-28M
actually used, I wondered if there was something going on when peak
memory demands forced a swap-file action. With Xitami, RealServer,
and a VNC service running, I'm now using 40M out of 128M physical,
so swapping just doesn't happen.

The TCP/IP stack in XP is totally new (actually lifted from one of
the PC unix distributions) and reportedly better. But I've been
happy enough with NT4's uptime that I have not cared to move to XP
(and it certainly would not be snappy on a P-100/32M).

 -PRR

Hi.
Probably it is just a typo. Mime section should be:

[Mime]
     Wbmp=image/vnd.wap.wbmp
     Wml=text/vnd.wap.wml
     Wmlc=application/vnd.wap.wmlc
     Wmls=text/vnd.wap.wmlscript
     Wmlsc=application/vnd.wap.wmlscriptc

You have one "e" more.
                                 Bye
                                         Zdenko.

I got it to work by re-installing Xitami and PHP (btw, on Windows 98
SE). I've changed the cgi.force_redirect to 0, without setting the
doc.root and then it works fine (but only used locally, because of
security-issues). I didn't have to make any further changes to the php.ini.

So you might try a fresh install.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr  5 13:45:57 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thon Becker)
Date: Fri, 5 Apr 2002 05:45:57 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] xirtual hosts
Message-ID: <014101c1dc9f$d57af340$86000344@ph.cox.net>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_013E_01C1DC65.28FA8980

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr  5 17:09:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (M. Jason Smiley)
Date: Fri, 5 Apr 2002 11:09:21 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Running multiple xitami on w2k
References: <E98C8F1ECF97D311BB320008C7E6D64202672359@END_MAIL>
Message-ID: <094101c1dcbc$3fe3ca60$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>

stop the xitami service running on port 80.
open the xitami WBA for the new service and change the "ip port base" from
"0" to "5000"
your new xitami service will then start on port 5080 (you may have to
stop/restart).
start the original service back up (it will still be on port 80)

i'm sure there's other ways to do this....

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr  5 17:21:24 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Claessen)
Date: Fri, 5 Apr 2002 10:21:24 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Running multiple xitami on w2k
References: <E98C8F1ECF97D311BB320008C7E6D64202672359@END_MAIL>
Message-ID: <004201c1dcbd$f398eda0$16dc9e84@pb.intersil.com>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_003B_01C1DC8B.A365B0C0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Quote from the FAQ:

"
50: I want several 'sites' on the same IP address, on different ports =20

You can run several copies of Xitami, each in a different directory, and =
each on a different port. Xitami is small enough that this will not slow =
down the system. In each directory, create a suitable defaults.cfg file =
with the server:portbase set to a different value.=20

"

The two keywords here are 'directory' and 'port'.
You will need to install TWO instances of Xitami,
in different directories, with a different port base,
and start the servers from their own respective directories.

Paul Claessen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr  5 19:42:59 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Claessen)
Date: Fri, 5 Apr 2002 12:42:59 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] HTTP Publishing
References: <5.1.0.14.0.20020405093258.00aa2ec0@eastexch1.wincoms.com>
Message-ID: <007e01c1dcd1$b6109460$16dc9e84@pb.intersil.com>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_007B_01C1DC9F.6AD77360
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

'PUT' requires that your client app has the capability to invoke that
request: most browsers don't. It also has MAJOR security issues.
AND you need a script at the server that actually deals with the
put request. Using the upload mechanism with 'POST' and the
'multipart' mime type is probably much easier (although it would
still require a CGI program and has security issues!).
But why bother, when Xitami has such a nice FTP server built in?
Not even sure if Xitami supports 'put' requests!

Anyway, although the following article is about Apache, it DOES
contain some noteworthy information about using 'put' requests.
http://www.apacheweek.com/features/put

Hope it helps,

Regards,
Paul Claessen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr  5 19:47:36 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ervin Kosch)
Date: Fri, 5 Apr 2002 13:47:36 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] HTTP Publishing
Message-ID: <200204051856.g35Iu4Y00457@japetos.host4u.net>

What your trying to do id use FrontPage extensions.  Xitami doesn't support
that protocal.  FP extensions is a special way to change files on a web
server.  I would recomend that you publish your pages with an FTP program.

Xitami does not now, nor will in the future support Front Page extensions. 
This has been a hot topic in the past.  If you're a savy enough programmer
Xitami is open source.  And the FrontPage is actually a documented protocal
so you could in theory build FP compatibility into Xitami.

--------- Original message --------

Ervin,

No, I don't think he's referring to Frontpage. Just to HTTP's
'put' request. (See RFC 2068, under 9.6).

Xitami indeed states somewhere that they have no intention
to support Frontpage and gives as reason that it is not properly
documented and that they're not in the business of reverse
engineering Microsoft software.

So, since you claim FP to be a documented protocol, I would
be very interested in obtaining a link to that document!
Could you supply that to us?

Kind Regards,
Paul Claessen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr  5 23:08:51 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Claessen)
Date: Fri, 5 Apr 2002 16:08:51 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] HTTP Publishing
References: <200204051856.g35Iu4Y00457@japetos.host4u.net> <5.1.0.14.0.20020405133108.00a92ec0@eastexch1.wincoms.com>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_00CF_01C1DCBC.2D0EEDC0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Sean,

Maybe this quote from the FAQ helps...:

"
15: I get 'Not authorized to access this resource' on other URLs =20

There are a number of specific reasons why Xitami may return this:=20

  1.. The resource you are accessing is protected by a 'webmask' =
definition which excludes your PC.=20
  2.. You are trying to browse a directory, but directory listings have =
not been enabled.=20
  3.. You are trying to use an HTTP update method (PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or =
COPY) on a resource which has not been authorised for this.=20
  4.. You are trying to run the WBA, but this has been disabled by the =
security:admin option.=20
  5.. The URL refers to a Windows short filename when a long filename =
also exists. Xitami rejects this as being a potential security =
violation. You can switch this behaviour off by setting =
security:safepaths to 0.=20
  6.. You're trying to do a HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation, =
and specified an absolute Content-Location: or Destination: URI which =
did not have the same path as the request URI. Xitami rejects this =
because the authorisation was carried-out on the request URL, and using =
a different path for the Content-Location: or Destination: URL would =
violate this.=20
  7.. A HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation failed because of an =
access violation at the operating system level - for instance Xitami =
tried to write to a file which was marked as read-only.=20
In most of these cases, the reason for the error will be logged when you =
enable server debugging.=20

"

Kind Regards,
Paul Claessen

  <LI>You are trying to use an HTTP update method (PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or =
COPY)=20
  on a resource which has not been authorised for this.=20
  <LI>You are trying to run the WBA, but this has been disabled by the=20
  security:admin option.=20
  <LI>The URL refers to a Windows short filename when a long filename =
also=20
  exists. Xitami rejects this as being a potential security violation. =
You can=20
  switch this behaviour off by setting security:safepaths to 0.=20
  <LI>You're trying to do a HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation, =
and=20
  specified an absolute Content-Location: or Destination: URI which did =
not have=20
  the same path as the request URI. Xitami rejects this because the=20
  authorisation was carried-out on the request URL, and using a =
different path=20
  for the Content-Location: or Destination: URL would violate this.=20
  <LI>A HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation failed because of an =
access=20
  violation at the operating system level - for instance Xitami tried to =
write=20
  to a file which was marked as read-only. </LI></OL>
<P>In most of these cases, the reason for the error will be logged when =
you=20
enable server debugging. </P></DIV>

size=3D2>"</FONT></DIV>

out the correct way to configure the xitami.aut allow an HTTP put. I've 
added http-update=1 to the xitami.aut file but it's not accepting it for my 
user I configured. Maybe someone has a xitami.aut file I can see who's 
using HTTP puts to the server.

>    * You're trying to do a HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation, and

> path for the Content-Location: or Destination: URL would violate this.

Content-Type: text/html; charset="us-ascii"

<html>
<br>
I believe my problem is that HTTP update method on a resource which has
not been authorized for this. I think it's authentication. I'm trying to
figure out the correct way to configure the xitami.aut allow an HTTP put.
I've added http-update=1 to the xitami.aut file but it's not accepting it
for my user I configured. Maybe someone has a xitami.aut file I can see
who's using HTTP puts to the server.<br><br>
Thanks,<br><br>
Sean<br><br>
At 04:08 PM 4/5/2002 -0600, you wrote:<br>
<blockquote type=cite class=cite cite><font face="Comic Sans MS" size=2 color="#800000">Sean,</font><br>
&nbsp;<br>
<font face="Comic Sans MS" size=2 color="#800000">Maybe this quote from
the FAQ helps...:</font><br>
&nbsp;<br>
<font face="Comic Sans MS" size=2 color="#800000">&quot;</font><br><br>
<b>15: I get 'Not authorized to access this resource' on other
URLs</b><a name="w_15"></a>  <br><br>
There are a number of specific reasons why Xitami may return this: 
<ol>
<li>The resource you are accessing is protected by a 'webmask' definition
which excludes your PC. 
<li>You are trying to browse a directory, but directory listings have not
been enabled. 
<li>You are trying to use an HTTP update method (PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or
COPY) on a resource which has not been authorised for this. 
<li>You are trying to run the WBA, but this has been disabled by the
security:admin option. 
<li>The URL refers to a Windows short filename when a long filename also
exists. Xitami rejects this as being a potential security violation. You
can switch this behaviour off by setting security:safepaths to 0. 
<li>You're trying to do a HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation, and
specified an absolute Content-Location: or Destination: URI which did not
have the same path as the request URI. Xitami rejects this because the
authorisation was carried-out on the request URL, and using a different
path for the Content-Location: or Destination: URL would violate this. 
<li>A HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation failed because of an
access violation at the operating system level - for instance Xitami
tried to write to a file which was marked as read-only. 
</ol>In most of these cases, the reason for the error will be logged when
you enable server debugging. <br>
<font face="Comic Sans MS" size=2 color="#800000">&quot;</font><br>
&nbsp;<br>
<font face="Comic Sans MS" size=2 color="#800000">Kind
Regards,</font><br>
<font face="Comic Sans MS" size=2 color="#800000">Paul
Claessen</font><br>

Sean,

Just tried this (see below) and it works!
Despite my earlier response, you don't need a special script=20
for it at the server.

Just had the following in my .aut file:

[/]
    all=3D*
    webmask=3D*
    http-update=3D1
    http-put=3D1

Let me know if that works for you too!

Kind Regards,
Paul

Just tried this and it works!
Despite my earlier response, you don't need a special script=20
for it at the server.

Just had the following in my .aut file:

[/]
    all=3D*
    webmask=3D*
    http-update=3D1
    http-put=3D1

Let me know if that works for you too!

Kind Regards,
Paul

  At 04:08 PM 4/5/2002 -0600, you wrote:

    Sean,
    =20
    Maybe this quote from the FAQ helps...:
    =20
    "

    15: I get 'Not authorized to access this resource' on other URLs=20

    There are a number of specific reasons why Xitami may return this:=20
      1.. The resource you are accessing is protected by a 'webmask' =
definition which excludes your PC.=20
      2.. You are trying to browse a directory, but directory listings =
have not been enabled.=20
      3.. You are trying to use an HTTP update method (PUT, DELETE, =
MOVE, or COPY) on a resource which has not been authorised for this.=20
      4.. You are trying to run the WBA, but this has been disabled by =
the security:admin option.=20
      5.. The URL refers to a Windows short filename when a long =
filename also exists. Xitami rejects this as being a potential security =
violation. You can switch this behaviour off by setting =
security:safepaths to 0.=20
      6.. You're trying to do a HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY =
operation, and specified an absolute Content-Location: or Destination: =
URI which did not have the same path as the request URI. Xitami rejects =
this because the authorisation was carried-out on the request URL, and =
using a different path for the Content-Location: or Destination: URL =
would violate this.=20
      7.. A HTTP PUT, DELETE, MOVE, or COPY operation failed because of =
an access violation at the operating system level - for instance Xitami =
tried to write to a file which was marked as read-only.=20
    In most of these cases, the reason for the error will be logged when =
you enable server debugging.=20
    "
    =20
    Kind Regards,
    Paul Claessen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 08:29:51 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 19:29:51 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] xirtual hosts
In-Reply-To: Message from "bernd hohmann" <xitami@conacom.de>
 of "Fri, 05 Apr 2002 11:59:30 +0100." <200204051000.MAA30962@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <200204070729.TAA12361@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <200204051000.MAA30962@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>, "bernd hohmann" wr
ites:
>i finally managed it to compile b5 under os/2 and tried this
>version in our multi-domain environment.
>works, but doesnt recognizes any of the vhosts so i have to
>implement my old patch from beta 4 again.

Do you have a setting for [server] webpages in your defaults.cfg file?
In theory the bug that caused that to override every virtual host
setting has been fixed, but I'm not 100% certain the fix made it into
2.5b5.

Debug mode will probably reveal if it recognises the virtual host name
or not, and if so which directory it is trying to use.  If it recognises
the virtual host name, but goes and uses the default directory, chances
are that there's still an issue with setting [server] webpages.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 08:41:10 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 19:41:10 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Server Being Flooded
In-Reply-To: Message from "Gregory Hart" <freastro@yahoo.com>
 of "Sat, 30 Mar 2002 16:17:34 PST." <002801c1d849$75fe5920$0200a8c0@geh>
Message-ID: <200204070741.TAA12984@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <002801c1d849$75fe5920$0200a8c0@geh>, "Gregory Hart" writes:
>    My server is being flooded with cgi requests. When I have about 60
>active connections, my computer crashes because Xitami is not able to
>completely close all the perl windows. How can I get Xitami to send a 413
>(This server cannot handle your request) or a 502 (This server is currently
>overloaded - please try again later) when it has more than 5 active
>connections? Thanks.

Xitami will do this automatically when the CGIs take "too long" to run;
but there's no way to configure it so that, eg, 5 simultaneous
connections will cause the "try again later" type message.

You might want to reduce the [CGI] Timeout value in this situation, so
that more of the CGIs are cancelled quickly and a server overloaded
message sent.  However it's not a perfect fix because all the CGIs will
still be launched.  

You might also want to consider something like LRWP instead of CGIs, as
it's able to answer requests quicker (much much less startup overhead).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 08:43:44 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 19:43:44 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Questions configuring Xitami
In-Reply-To: Message from "WhiteShepherd" <fuzzydog@whiteshepherd.net>
 of "Sat, 30 Mar 2002 15:16:07 EST." <3CA5D6B7.30198.163F21E@localhost>
Message-ID: <200204070743.TAA13058@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3CA5D6B7.30198.163F21E@localhost>, "WhiteShepherd" writes:
>One: some of those connecting will be broadband connections.  Won't the 
>broadband connections take the lion share of the bandwidth (being able to 
>take more faster in shorter time frame) leaving the dialups with the scraps 
>of what they can down feed in a bandwidth crunch?  

You might want to experiment with the bandwidth shaping code in the Xitami
2.5 beta.  Read up on the pipe definitions files for how to do this.
That way you can limit connections to, say, a modem-and-a-bit worth
each, or something like that.

>My second question is I saw in the faq that EMX was limited to 40 open 
>sockets in the faq.  This has been in the faq for a LONG time.  Has the 
>newer versions of EMX made improvements on this?  

This is 40 sockets per process.  And it's just a default setting.  You
can tell EMX to allow space for more sockets for the process at runtime
by setting an environment variable; look at the EMX documentation for
details.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 08:46:29 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

Subject: [Xitami] Distributed?
In-Reply-To: Message from Matt Hunter <matt@canexus.com>
 of "Fri, 29 Mar 2002 14:18:28 EST." <5.1.0.14.0.20020329141428.03c06a30@canexus.com>
Message-ID: <200204070746.TAA13183@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.1.0.14.0.20020329141428.03c06a30@canexus.com>, Matt Hunter writes:
>I don't know how many of you are familiar with mod_backhand for the apache 
>server, but it allows you to have a cluster of servers with one master 
>server that handles all incoming connections.  Based on how busy each 
>machine is in the cluster, backhand decides if the master machine should 
>handle the request, or if it should redirect the request to another machine...

Sounds very clever.  (I've never used it, but I help look after some
sites that are getting to a point where something like that would be
useful.)

>Is there anything like this available for use with Xitami on a windows 
>platform??

Xitami doesn't have any equivilent of Apache's mod_proxy code (to talk
to a backend server, and then pass the results back) yet.  So no,
there's nothing in there to do load balancing like that.

You could possibly run Apache at the front and Xitami at the back
though.

FWIW, I've been thinking for a while that Xitami would be quite a good
choice for some proxy/load balancing code like this.  So in the unlikely
event that I get some free time (or the slightly more likely event that
there's actually a paying client that wants it), it might get written.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 08:51:36 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 19:51:36 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] HELP! web based admin problem?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Russel Olinger" <rolinger@airpower.net>
 of "Wed, 27 Mar 2002 15:13:31 PST." <03df01c1d5e5$02eae4a0$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <200204070751.TAA13295@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <03df01c1d5e5$02eae4a0$020aa8c0@Master>, "Russel Olinger" writes:
>I just posted my server live and I am hosting 8 different Vitual 
>Domains.  I want each domain to have the ability to administer itself 
>and nothing else.  However, when I go to the /admin for each domain they 
>all have full access to all admin privelages to ALL domains.  Big 
>security problem, obviously.

/admin is administration of the _whole_server_.  It should be restricted
to people that you trust.  It's typically accessible automatically under
each domain name, by default.  But you _may_ be able to turn it off on a
domain-by-domain basis (I can't remember if the code checks this at the
right place for that to work).

Generally it'd be best not to allow anyone you don't trust running
anything they like on your server access to /admin, because with /admin
access they can set it up to let them run any program they like on your
server.

Most places I've worked configuration of the webserver (rather than just
uploading content) is restricted to a single webserver admin.  And they
double check things for security reasons, etc, before adding new setups.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 08:55:45 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 19:55:45 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] REMOTE_USER being lost - urgent
In-Reply-To: Message from "Becky R. Izen - MSSP" <bizen@jfsmssp.org>
 of "Tue, 19 Mar 2002 10:43:19 PST." <3C971647.12443.10300F9@localhost>
Message-ID: <200204070755.TAA13496@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C971647.12443.10300F9@localhost>, "Becky R. Izen - MSSP" writes:
>Whenever they make an entry, I use the REMOTE_USER variable to capture which 
>employee is doing the work.  Up until March 5, this was working fine.  
>However, on March 5th I created an SSL certificate (private) and issued it 
>to everyone so everyone would be logging in via HTTPS.  

The REMOTE_USER setting comes from the HTTP authentication (ie, password
protected directories); it sounds to me like you've changed from HTTP 
authentication to some other authentication (eg, the HTTPS
certificate), so the REMOTE_USER value isn't being set.  You'll probably
need to change your script so that it extracts the user from the other
authentication method.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 08:56:44 2002

In-Reply-To: Message from "Stan Schretter" <schrette@verizon.net>
 of "Mon, 18 Mar 2002 22:45:39 EST." <000d01c1cef8$89cded30$037ba8c0@pooh>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 09:08:20 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 20:08:20 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Possible race condition in Xitami's temporary files module
In-Reply-To: Message from "Dmitry Isakbayev" <dmitry@transnexus.com>
 of "Sat, 16 Mar 2002 11:26:19 EST." <NEBBIJGPHKNLMOCJIHFJIEIDDAAA.dmitry@transnexus.com>
Message-ID: <200204070808.UAA14096@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NEBBIJGPHKNLMOCJIHFJIEIDDAAA.dmitry@transnexus.com>, "Dmitry Isakbayev" writes:
>If there might be a bug in the way Xitami handles temporary files, how can
>we avoid using them?

If you can recompile Xitami for your platform, and are willing to spare
some memory, then you can change the constant that triggers when a LRWP
response will be spooled to disk.  The relevant compile time constant is
BIG_RESPONSE_LEN in xilrwp.c; the default setting is 16384, ie 16KB.  If
you make this, say, 1048576, then up to 1MB will be held in memory.  (If
you're server is busy and sending a lot of large responses, then
obviously you'll need to have a lot of memory available.)

>How can I learn more about the way Xitami uses temporary files and generates
>temporary file names?

Unfortunately the only real documentation for this internal stuff is the
source code.  Most of it is smthttpl.c IIRC, although the main control
logic is in smthttp.c, and the thread of execution pops in and out
between the two of them.

For LRWPs the main thing to remember is that once the response is
received from the LRWP program it's basically treated like a CGI
response.  (The same is true for filter responses BTW.)

The temporary files are created in smthttpl.c in the CGI case, and
xilrwp.c in the LRWP case.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 09:10:55 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 20:10:55 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Password timeout?
In-Reply-To: Message from "AOK Lansing" <aoklans@tir.com>
 of "Thu, 14 Mar 2002 15:23:01 CDT." <002901c1cb96$0b8b5c60$0e20d943@bobh>
Message-ID: <200204070810.UAA14229@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <002901c1cb96$0b8b5c60$0e20d943@bobh>, "AOK Lansing" writes:
>Is there anyway to make a user re-enter their Username and Password after
>some time period. I would like to make the user re-enter their password if
>they have left a page and have not re-visited the same page for more than
>ten minutes.

It is the browser that caches the username/password, and avoids them
having to enter it again.  The only way to "delete" something from that
cache is to fail the authentication once (send back the appropriate HTTP
response for "authentication failed; try again").

If you're doing this with a script, then you might be able to do that
based on time.

A number of sites use their own login forms, and HTTP Cookies (which can
have timeouts) for basically this reason.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr  7 09:19:42 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 07 Apr 2002 20:19:42 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Help: Virutal Host !!
In-Reply-To: Message from "Joshi, Sunit" <sjoshi@ingr.com>
 of "Wed, 06 Mar 2002 08:30:55 MDT." <2C61CCE8A870D211A523080009B94E43071C78F9@HQ5>
Message-ID: <200204070819.UAA14737@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <2C61CCE8A870D211A523080009B94E43071C78F9@HQ5>, "Joshi, Sunit" writes:
>1)Create a virtual host called PyCgi so that it points to E:\\Sunit\\XMLFiles\\
>PyXml\\Scripts
>2)Be able to point to http://localhost/PyCgi/PyTest.py and runmy python scripts

You want a CGI-BIN directory.  It's going to be called "PyCGI" in the
URL, and have the appropriate directory as its on-disk location.  You'll
also need to enable index-pages-in-CGI-directory.

Something like:

[server]
  cgi-bin=E:/Sunit/XMLFiles/PyXml/Scripts
  cgi-url=/PyCGI

[cgi]
  mixed-url=1

You may also want to define some more default filenames to apply when
accessing a directory.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

It works at the DNS level rather than the server level.

>From the FAQ:

How do I balance load among my web servers?
I have 50 identical servers running on IP addresses
1.2.3.150, 1.2.3.151, and so on.
I'd like to spread www.heaven.af.mil requests among those servers.
Answer:
For versions 1.04 and above:
Simply put all 50 addresses into data.
tinydns will automatically return a random set of 8 addresses
for each request.
For versions 1.03 and below:
Delegate www.heaven.af.mil to
pickdns.

> Hello everyone!
> 
> I'm new to the mailing list, so please bare with any "stupid" or repeated
> questions I may have :-)
> 
> First question: is there an archive of this mailing list, so I can browse it
> before I ask a question?
> 
> Second: I've tried using ISAPI DLLs using the ISAPI daemon provided at
> www.xitami.com. The example ISAPI module ran fine (to my surprise, without
> the need of installing PWS/IIS). However, running one of my own ISAPI
> modules (written in Delphi 5) or PHP's ISAPI module, I get an error
> indicating the ISAPI module could not be loaded with error 126. I installed
> PWS and tried again just to be sure, but to no avail. Is this a known
> limitation or...?
> 
> Perhaps someone could point me out to my main goal actually: I've got PHP on
> the system, which is simply a filter for .PHP pages to the PHP executable.
> When enabling a few PHP extension DLLs, running the executable on each
> request increases the response time. So therefore I wanted to use the ISAPI
> version instead, because the extension DLLs wouldn't need to be loaded with
> each request. But it haven't gotten it to work like that so far :-(
> 
> FYI: My Xitami web server is running on Windows NT 4.0 Workstation with SRP6
> (Rollup)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 10 03:38:28 2002

Can anyone recommend a good ftp server?

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 10 04:01:53 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Joe Byrne)
Date: Tue, 9 Apr 2002 22:01:53 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] FTP server
References: <200204091442.QAA06965@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net> <OE64rbmaMxbfOzlWbd80001546a@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <019901c1e03c$11960af0$f6fea8c0@jjb>

Sure...just finished 2 months of intense testing of most of the popular FTP
servers.  Here are my results:

Fastest (by far) although a bit hard to configure:
http://www.raidenftpd.com/  $13.00US standard version
Easiest to get running and very stable:  http://www.texis.com/ $30.00US
Best free server with plenty of options and easy to use:
http://www.nitrolic.com/  (free)
Longest history, stable, good options, reasonably priced:
http://www.serv-u.com  $39.95US

--Joe

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 10 04:15:40 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Joe Byrne)
Date: Tue, 9 Apr 2002 22:15:40 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] FTP server
References: <200204091442.QAA06965@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net> <OE64rbmaMxbfOzlWbd80001546a@hotmail.com> <159601c1e03c$9170c170$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>
Message-ID: <01a501c1e03d$fe49f090$f6fea8c0@jjb>

> ftp server??? if you're on this list... don't you have xitami?<

Actually, I think a lot of us found the FTP service in Xitami to be...well,
not so stable.  Xitami is a great web server, that's what it is and that's
what it does best...FTP is something totally different and it only makes
sense to get a real FTP server that does...well, file transfers :)

> or do you mean ftp client? in that case - i recommend ws-ftp

Up until this last release (v7) I would have agreed with you, but Ipswich
really blew it with this one.  They've tried to put to much into a stable
product just for an upgrade and ended up with a 'feature-rich' program that
is very unstable.  Within the first 45 days of its release they had 9
updates....shades of MS.  To bad too, WSFTP was a great piece of work
before.

--Joe

I don't know what you're looking for, but I would consider Xitami a good ftp
server. There is also Argo Software's FTP server, but I don't think it is as
good. You can also just look at download.com for an ftp server, but make
sure that you filter out anything that is not free.

Argo Software <http://argosoft.com>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 10 18:29:55 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (WhiteShepherd)
Date: Wed, 10 Apr 2002 13:29:55 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Security, Counters, and CGI
Message-ID: <3CB43E53.3005.1E3572D7@localhost>


     Well I got the OS/2 version of Xitami running and have been looking for a good 
counter.  My decision came down some tight parameters.  I didn't want a "counter 
service" that could track and spam my users or web page with their logos.  I looked at 
Java and Java script.  But Java often makes browsers especially running on MS 
systems unstable.  I didn't want to enable #EXEC as I did not want the security hole. 
What I wanted something that was "simple" and self contained cgi (ie a cgi I can modify 
and put in without having to install a lot of other stuff).  Finally a cgi that would not count 
reloads.  

     To bad I was not able to find a function in Xitami to count web pages. :/  After two 
days of searching I came across graph counter.  It covered three of the 4 "hoped for" 
functions.  It was simple (needing only 2 edited lines in the cgi file), was completely self 
contained (needed no extra installed graphic handlers), and could be launched by a 
IMG link.  

     I edited and installed the cgi counter script and it counted just fine launching the 
script directly from the browser:  http://www.furtopia.org/cgi-bin/counter.cgi     However 
when I place the IMG link ( IMG SCR="http://www.furtopia.org/cgi-bin/counter.cgi?0" ) 
into the web page I get a broken link.  The CGI "IS" running when the web page is 
accessed as the count test file does go up.  It just displays a broken link for the image.  

     Any ideas as to what may cause this?  I was beginning to wonder if it was a 
configuration setting in Xitami I missed or just the script?  If you want to look at the cgi I 
am trying to use I have placed it here: http://www.furtopia.org/cgi  if anyone is curious.  

   WhiteShepherd (Gene Angel)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 10 19:08:55 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brad Smith)
Date: Wed, 10 Apr 2002 14:08:55 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Security, Counters, and CGI
In-Reply-To: <3CB43E53.3005.1E3572D7@localhost>
Message-ID: <3CB44777.9141.89E0D9@localhost>

Your URL should read:

<IMG SRC="http://www.furtopia.org/cgi-bin/counter.cgi?something.gif">

If it ends in a graphical suffix, that will "trick" web browsers.

Brad Smith
Social Design Technologies

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 10 20:14:08 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 10 Apr 2002 15:14:08 -0400
Subject: Re[2]: [Xitami] Security, Counters, and CGI
In-Reply-To: <3CB452E1.5175.1E85BE9C@localhost>
References: <3CB43E53.3005.1E3572D7@localhost>
 <3CB452E1.5175.1E85BE9C@localhost>

Works for me in MSIE 6.0 and in NetScape 4.7.

I am directly opening http://www.furtopia.org/cgi-bin/counter.cgi?0

Do you have it embedded in a public web page that we can see? It may
work different inside an IMG tag than called directly.

NS47 says "has the following structure:

     http://www.furtopia.org/cgi-bin/counter.cgi?0
          Image: http://www.furtopia.org/digits/4.gif
          Image: http://www.furtopia.org/digits/7.gif "

And for the first image:

Location:  http://www.furtopia.org/digits/4.gif
 File MIME Type:  image/gif

So either you are sending a correct MIME header, or NS is making the
right guess based either on extension or the header of the actual
file.

 -PRR

Yup, that fails to show the counter in IE. NS is even more
erratic... one time I got only half the big dog, and NS was trying
to contact a server named "math..." which isn't in your HTML.

Yet if I copy the IMG link and paste it to your domain name, it
loads fine.

There seem to be a lot of BIG, FONT, and SMALL tags in the bottom
line of text. Trying to be sure they were nested correctly, I ran
out of fingers. NS is prone to go wacky if you throw too many font
attributes together. That "shouldn't" affect how it handles an IMG
tag, but... no, it does not matter. I trimmed your HTML down to one
word, no tags, and it still fails.

What language is the script? If you rename it counter.gif, it may
work better. I name my Perl scripts that return images with a GIF
extension. Xitami opens them and finds the #!/foo/bar/perl line, and
feeds them through Perl before sending them to the client.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr 12 04:18:35 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (WhiteShepherd)
Date: Thu, 11 Apr 2002 23:18:35 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] hack attack or just ignorance?
In-Reply-To: <MABBILGNLFGMJIPJLFFKKECICCAA.bronder@attbi.com>
Message-ID: <3CB619CB.18721.2576E8D6@localhost>

     It is either a script to try and hack vulnerable systems or a denial of service attack on 
someone else.  If it is a denial of service attack your IP would of been picked out by a IP 
port scanner.  You and your bandwidth (as well as many others) are are now the 
unwilling participant of a denial of service attack against someone else.  

     In basic form a hacker/worm sends out a packet with a "faked" IP that makes it's way 
to your web server (notice the IP in your log is most likely the victim's IP) .  Your server 
thinking someone is trying to connect sends back a response.  The victims IP cannot 
respond so all servers used as relays sends out 4 packets to the victims IP for every 1 
faked packet they get.  Denial of service attacks are becoming more and more common 
as "kits" begin to spread and new changes are made in windows.  

     There is only two ways of stopping this that I know of (aside from fixing MS security 
flaws).  The best solution would be ISP's block non originating "faked" IP packets.  This 
would kill a mountain of abuse over night.  But it may have to get even worse before the 
major ISP's are forced to change.  The other alternative is to have your server stop 
sending to a IP for say an hour to any server that can't be contacted on initial contact or 
after 3 contacts (or whatever tries).  There may be better ways around this problem.  I 
don't know if the new Xitami can shield itself from this kind of abuse.  But it would be a 
nice feature.

  WhiteShepherd (Gene Angel)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr 12 17:15:36 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 12 Apr 2002 12:15:36 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] hack attack or just ignorance?
In-Reply-To: <MABBILGNLFGMJIPJLFFKKECICCAA.bronder@attbi.com>
References: <MABBILGNLFGMJIPJLFFKKECICCAA.bronder@attbi.com>
Message-ID: <18471629777.20020412121536@rci.rutgers.edu>

> These aren't malicious attempts are they?

They are, and they come from within your ISP, but probably not
"from" your ISP. The IP number translates to a hostname that looks a
lot like the one you sent this email from.

 > host 24.128.72.232
232.72.128.24.IN-ADDR.ARPA domain name pointer h00c0f03820eb.ne.client2.attbi.com

 > host 24.128.19.74
 74.19.128.24.IN-ADDR.ARPA domain name pointer h00a0cc58ab25.ne.client2.attbi.com

What are they doing?

 "GET /scripts/..%c1%9c../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+dir

This requested URL is "malformed". The dots and percents aren't
right. Xitami properly notices that, and replies 404 or 403
depending on just where it decides that this is meaningless.

However, MS IIS webserver is tricked into navigating up out of the
webpages folder, into the root, down into the windows system folder,
and runs CMD, the command processor! (Some call it the "DOS box".)

This involves two very stupid mistakes by MS IIS's programmers.
Malformed URLs should be rejected, and files outside those folder
specifically designated for web-serving should never be served. You
could say that running a program not designated for CGI delivery is
also a mistake, though MS IIS's notion of CGI is pretty elaborate,
supporting MS-proprietary extensions that basically sell MS
programming languages.

In this case, they request a DIR from CMD. On Xitami and patched
IIS, the response is "error", they ignore it. If the response is a
list of files, they struck gold. They can put more clever commands
into CMD and do almost anything to your machine.

You may wonder why they are trying IIS hacks on your Xitami server.
Well, IIS is the second most common webserver, and THE most common
inside home-ISP networks. Many folks have IIS running and don't even
know it. And it is just plain easier to try a IIS-hack on every
machine than to actually check which ones are IIS. Typically, the
script contacts -every- IP number in a given range, whether or not
there is a webserver there. If no server, it times-out. If a "good"
webserver, it ignores these silly requests. But unpatched IIS will
do the wrong thing quickly and efficiently.

This isn't a DoS attack. CMD..DIR just asks for a list of files. If
they can do that, they can ask CMD to install software that could
start flooding other machines to jam them. But that's not seen here.

You could report that IP number to your ISP. It is barely possible
that your ISP is doing it: my net-admins do a similar (but better!)
scan every month and inform anybody hosting a vulnerable machine.
More likely it is some kid reading hacker-sites and trying the most
basic hack-scripts. If the ISP cares, they will warn the account
holder and the kid may be sent to bed without supper. But there is
always another kid.

It does you no harm, except a slight increase in log-file size. When
CodeRed was popular, my logs were 10% real hits and 90% CodeRed
errors. In the peak-week, it actually was a mild problem: my slow
machine was bogged on logs, and I had to take it down for 10 minutes
and delete some monster files. CodeRed and Samba are different: they
use a VERY long request URL (thousands of characters) to overflow
IIS's request buffer and inject malicious code into IIS. Again,
Xitami handles this correctly: no overflow, just an error and huge
log files.

>  Perl.exe mysteriously disappeared from my machine recently.

Odd. But not something a hacker would want to do.

 -PRR


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Apr 13 02:36:36 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael Bronder)
Date: Fri, 12 Apr 2002 21:36:36 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] hack attack or just ignorance?
References: <MABBILGNLFGMJIPJLFFKKECICCAA.bronder@attbi.com> <18471629777.20020412121536@rci.rutgers.edu>
Message-ID: <001901c1e28b$a71cd260$0400a8c0@com>

Well... this is all pretty far out.  Thanks everyone for the comprehensive
responses.

2 questions then...

1) It seems that all of these requests come through with a GET request.  Is
there a way that Xitami can block any of those, as I don't expect anyone
coming to call with that as a gift.

2) everyone's responses essentially say "don't worry, you can tell by the
error code that they're not getting in" which is great, but is there another
alarm that will tip me off if someone has made it in?  Any decent resources
for info on web server security?

Thanks all,

mb


----- Original Message -----
From: "Paul Reid" <preid@rci.rutgers.edu>
To: "Michael Bronder" <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Friday, April 12, 2002 12:15 PM
Subject: Re: [Xitami] hack attack or just ignorance?


> > These aren't malicious attempts are they?
>
> They are, and they come from within your ISP, but probably not
> "from" your ISP. The IP number translates to a hostname that looks a
> lot like the one you sent this email from.
>
>  > host 24.128.72.232
> 232.72.128.24.IN-ADDR.ARPA domain name pointer
h00c0f03820eb.ne.client2.attbi.com
>
>  > host 24.128.19.74
>  74.19.128.24.IN-ADDR.ARPA domain name pointer
h00a0cc58ab25.ne.client2.attbi.com
>
> What are they doing?
>
>  "GET /scripts/..%c1%9c../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+dir
>
> This requested URL is "malformed". The dots and percents aren't
> right. Xitami properly notices that, and replies 404 or 403
> depending on just where it decides that this is meaningless.
>
> However, MS IIS webserver is tricked into navigating up out of the
> webpages folder, into the root, down into the windows system folder,
> and runs CMD, the command processor! (Some call it the "DOS box".)
>
> This involves two very stupid mistakes by MS IIS's programmers.
> Malformed URLs should be rejected, and files outside those folder
> specifically designated for web-serving should never be served. You
> could say that running a program not designated for CGI delivery is
> also a mistake, though MS IIS's notion of CGI is pretty elaborate,
> supporting MS-proprietary extensions that basically sell MS
> programming languages.
>
> In this case, they request a DIR from CMD. On Xitami and patched
> IIS, the response is "error", they ignore it. If the response is a
> list of files, they struck gold. They can put more clever commands
> into CMD and do almost anything to your machine.
>
> You may wonder why they are trying IIS hacks on your Xitami server.
> Well, IIS is the second most common webserver, and THE most common
> inside home-ISP networks. Many folks have IIS running and don't even
> know it. And it is just plain easier to try a IIS-hack on every
> machine than to actually check which ones are IIS. Typically, the
> script contacts -every- IP number in a given range, whether or not
> there is a webserver there. If no server, it times-out. If a "good"
> webserver, it ignores these silly requests. But unpatched IIS will
> do the wrong thing quickly and efficiently.
>
> This isn't a DoS attack. CMD..DIR just asks for a list of files. If
> they can do that, they can ask CMD to install software that could
> start flooding other machines to jam them. But that's not seen here.
>
> You could report that IP number to your ISP. It is barely possible
> that your ISP is doing it: my net-admins do a similar (but better!)
> scan every month and inform anybody hosting a vulnerable machine.
> More likely it is some kid reading hacker-sites and trying the most
> basic hack-scripts. If the ISP cares, they will warn the account
> holder and the kid may be sent to bed without supper. But there is
> always another kid.
>
> It does you no harm, except a slight increase in log-file size. When
> CodeRed was popular, my logs were 10% real hits and 90% CodeRed
> errors. In the peak-week, it actually was a mild problem: my slow
> machine was bogged on logs, and I had to take it down for 10 minutes
> and delete some monster files. CodeRed and Samba are different: they
> use a VERY long request URL (thousands of characters) to overflow
> IIS's request buffer and inject malicious code into IIS. Again,
> Xitami handles this correctly: no overflow, just an error and huge
> log files.
>
> >  Perl.exe mysteriously disappeared from my machine recently.
>
> Odd. But not something a hacker would want to do.
>
>  -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Apr 13 03:06:23 2002

In-Reply-To: <001901c1e28b$a71cd260$0400a8c0@com>

I'd recommend a good firewall like Zona Alarm (free) or Norton 
Personal firewall.  You can stealth all ports except those you use and if 
any application wants to use the network you must give it permission 
first by creating a "rule" to let it run in the future.  It's not perfect security 
but better than nothing.

   WhiteShepherd (Gene Angel)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 15 11:58:27 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Patricko)
Date: Mon, 15 Apr 2002 04:58:27 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] SSI #exec
References: <00a001c1e01c$30156860$6fb14cd8@euman> <00af01c1e43a$0b1c6190$f6fea8c0@jjb>
Message-ID: <026d01c1e46c$794aa320$62643718@Patricko>

[Ssi]
    Enabled = "1"
    Exec = "1"

Can't you put a Shortcut to xitami.cpl on your desktop or in your
Launch bar? A "CPL" file is really just an EXE file.

I'm not at an Xitami machine but I can do this:

Start, Settings, Control Panel.

Right-click on Mouse (or Xitami?), an option is "Create Shortcut".
Do that, it tell you that the shortcut is created on the Desktop (I
guess it does not want ControlPanel directory cluttered).

Now find your Desktop, drag the Mouse shortcut to the LaunchBar
(normally populated with IE and Outlook). I click that and I can
twiddle my mouse's properties.

Same should work for the Xitami CPL ?

I just noticed that the SSI include tag (e.g. the one on the testssi 
page <!--#include file="testssi.inc"-->) cuases the rest of the 
including document (e.g. testssi.ssi) after the tag not to get delivered 
if the included document itself uses SSI as the example include does.

SSI returns just fine if the included document itself does not try any 
SSI calls.

This is true using Xitami 2.5b5 (and 2.5b4) with NS6.1, 4.7 and IE5 and 
appears to be a xitami thing in that the HTML is in fact completely 
unfinished. I'm guessing that Xixssi doesn't deal well with the same 
page requiring 2 levels of return.

Also in the process of debugging and playing I noticed that Xitami has a 
limit on files with SSI includes of about 35,000+ bytes (one file 
displayed upto the 35922nd byte, another upto the 35553rd) and any data 
thereafter is abruptly truncated. The limit is not there for pure HTML 
files - I can successfully read 1Mbyte + sized .htm files but the same 
file renamed as .SSI will be truncated around this point even if it has 
no includes.

Francis

Let this *Click* represent the lightbulb of understanding over my 
head.  

You are correct.  It certainly looks like Xitami stores the entire text 
into a single limited variable (tsk tsk).  Whoever assigned that 
variable certainly wanted to keep a very small footprint.

I misunderstood because I've been generating pages of text from 
scripts using the ssi EXEC command and not the INCLUDE 
command.  This method allows huge megabytes of sculpted text 
which can be nested in dynamic files.  I don't think there's a limit to 
the number of EXEC calls you can make in a single document.

I wonder if any server that would allow you to *include* very large 
(mb) text files would also a security risk when they slow or crash 
doing memory manipulation.  Does IIS allow larger includes?

My guess is that Xitami also prefers outside scripts and software to 
take the memory and security risks so that the server doesn't crash 
~ like the scripts many people write.

~Michael

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Apr 16 16:15:40 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (bernd hohmann)
Date: Tue, 16 Apr 2002 16:15:40 +0100 (MEZ)
Subject: [Xitami] Denial of Service Attacks?
In-Reply-To: <002b01c1e549$f59c0260$4c20d943@bobh>
Message-ID: <200204161416.QAA11586@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

On Tue, 16 Apr 2002 09:23:53 -0400, AOK Lansing wrote:

> Please excuse my ignorance. Can someone please explain exactly what a Denial
> of Service attack is and how I can determine if someone has is trying to
> send one to my Xitami server?

a DoS is usually a type of attack on a network to bring the
network to its knees by flooding it with useless traffic.

a DDoS (distributed denial of service attack) is something
different: in the first step, a software tries to break into
your computer to install a software which tries to replicate to
other victim computers. if there are enough infected computers,
all machines starts a DoS to a specific server.

Nimda and CodeRed are such DDoS worms who used a security leak
in the IIS for breaking in and distributing itself.

Xitami (as far as understand) there are no such leaks.

bernd

----- Original Message -----
From: "Michael" <michael@alft.net>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Tuesday, April 16, 2002 9:10 AM
Subject: Re: [Xitami] Changing web page filesize limit




From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Apr 16 18:32:06 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 16 Apr 2002 13:32:06 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Denial of Service Attacks?
In-Reply-To: <002b01c1e549$f59c0260$4c20d943@bobh>
References: <002b01c1e549$f59c0260$4c20d943@bobh>
Message-ID: <37821820365.20020416133206@rci.rutgers.edu>

> exactly what a Denial of Service attack is and how I can determine
> if someone has is trying to send one to my Xitami server?

Pretend that I hate you or your website.

So much, that I come over to your place with a big axe and cut your
wire, maybe axe your machine to pieces.

That's a Denial of Service (DoS) attack. I have Denied you and/or
your clients the Service that you were providing.

Of course axing-up a PC is hard work. And I don't know where you
are. And you might have a 100 pound dog sleeping in your computer
room.

So I let my computer do my dirty work.

One way is to find a back door on your machine, where I can slip in
and delete files or install my own malicious program to corrupt or
wipe your machine.

Another way to make your web service unavailable, without knowing
any backdoor on your machine, would be to run a program on my
machine that *constantly* requested pages or files from your
machine. If I do enough of that, all other users will have a very
hard time using your service.

But if I'm on dial-up modem, and you have Portal-Class servers and
connection to the network backbone, I can request all I can and you
may never even notice the silly "attack". And I've lost the use of
my own machine and connection while it is busy trying to over-load
your machine.

So hackers enlist other people's machines to help. Many Windows
machines have no passwords, and it is easy to install programs on
them. Windows often has unpatched loopholes. Also, many people will
open any darn thing they fine in their mailbox, so I send them my
malicious program and some of them will run it. If I can get 100
other machines to keep your machine busy, your machine has a very
high load and my machine isn't being used at all. And the attack
does not trace back to me.

Variations of these tricks have thrown -thousands- of "innocent"
machines against the US White House server and GRC's site. Both were
able to dodge the attack, either in advance or by a long night of
hasty network configuration. But it wasn't any fun for them.

There seem to be an endless stream of new variants of DoS attacks.
If a DNS server can be hacked, all requests for one site may end up
at some other site. My school has been getting hit at the black-box
machine that connects us to the outside world.

So there isn't any single thing to look for, to show that you may be
under DoS attack. The best hacks leave no traces. Even if your
machine does stop working, it may not be easy to know if it was an
outside attack or something wrong in the machine.

 -PRR

Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="livecnt1.pl"

	filename="livecnt1.pl"

#! d:/perl/bin/perl


$sURLFilter       =3D '';
$sIPFilter        =3D '';
$sHostFilter      =3D '';
$sCounterFilter   =3D '';
$bAutoCreate      =3D 0;


#------------------------------------------------------------------------=
---

{
  local( $__COUNTER_DAT ) =3D 'livecntr.dat';

  print "Content-type: text/plain\nPragma: no-cache\nCache-control: =
no-cache\nExpires: Mon, 28 Apr 1997 00:01:00 -0500\n\n";


  if( $ARGV[0] )
  {
    local( $nCount ) =3D 0;
    local( $Temp );

    if( '' ne $ARGV[4] )
    {
      $ENV{'HTTP_REFERER'} =3D $ARGV[4];
    }

    if( $ARGV[1] && ( '0' ne $ARGV[1] ) )
    {
      $__COUNTER_DAT =3D $ARGV[1] . '.lcd';
    }

    if( -w "$__COUNTER_DAT" )
    {
      local( $bInc ) =3D 0;

      if( open( F, "+<$__COUNTER_DAT" ) )
      {
        #flock( F, 2 );
        seek( F, 0, 0 );

        ( $Temp, $nCount ) =3D split( /\s/, <F> );

        if( 'i' eq $ARGV[0] )
        {
          local( $bFiltersOk ) =3D 1;

          if( $sURLFilter && ( lc( $ENV{'HTTP_REFERER'} ) !~ $sURLFilter =
) )
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }
          if( $bFiltersOk     &&
              $sIPFilter      && ( $ENV{'REMOTE_ADDR'} =3D~ $sIPFilter ) =
)
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }
          if( $bFiltersOk     &&
              $sHostFilter    && ( $ENV{'REMOTE_HOST'} =3D~ $sHostFilter =
) )
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }
          if( $bFiltersOk     &&
              $sCounterFilter && ( $__COUNTER_DAT =3D~ $sCounterFilter ) =
)
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }

          if( $bFiltersOk )
          {
            seek( F, 0, 0 );

            ++$nCount;

            print F "Total: $nCount\n";

            $bInc =3D 1;
          }
        }

        #flock( F, 8 );
        close( F );
      }

    }
    elsif( $bAutoCreate )=20
    {
      if( ( !( -e "$__COUNTER_DAT" ) ) && open( F, ">$__COUNTER_DAT" ) )
      {
        print F "Total: 0\n";
        close( F );
      }
    }

    print "c0=3D$nCount\n";
    if( 'v' eq $ARGV[0] )
    {
      print "vr=3D99AX\n";
    }
  }
}

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 17 13:12:22 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 17 Apr 2002 14:12:22 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] CGI arguments passing (newbee question)
References: <NGBBJAFHALILDOAFEDNAEEDJCAAA.egbert@familie-egberts.tk>
Message-ID: <3CBD66A6.2050504@freesbee.fr>

E. Egberts wrote:

>Hi,
>
>I'm trying to implement a couple of Perl scripts which expect their
>arguments in the $ARGV array. Can I configure the Xitami web server (version
>2.4d9) such that arguments are passed through this array in stead of the CGI
>envirionment variable QUERY_STRING?
>
No.

However it should be relatively trivial to parse either <STDIN> or 
$ENV{'QUERY_STRING'} to create a suitable array. The problem is that the 
output of a program that uses a CLI fo its arguments is unlikely to 
suitable for display on a webserver as it won't generate HTML. What you 
probably need to do is create a wrapper progrm (using for example the 
CGI.pm library) that you can then wrap around all these scripts.

Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 17 21:20:48 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Russel Olinger)
Date: Wed, 17 Apr 2002 13:20:48 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Denial of Service Attacks?
References: <002b01c1e549$f59c0260$4c20d943@bobh>
Message-ID: <06d101c1e64d$5ce13d60$030000c0@Master>

The most sophisticated type of attack is a Smurf DoS.  To Smurf is to change
the source IP address of every out going packet and then hit someones server
with hundreds or thousands of packets per second.    When someone is
Smurfing you, its nearly impossible to track them down because every packet
has a false source address, and each false address is different from the
previous one.  The most common form of a Smurf DoS is a "Syn" attack.

A "syn" is a tcp packet one computer sends to another to initiate a
communication of some sort, the recipient computer gets the "syn", checks
the source address of that syn and then responds with an "ack" (ack =
acknowledgement), completing the handshake and then both computers start
talking and listening to each other.  However, years ago, most computers
only had a buffer to handle up to, maybe, 200 "syn"s per second.  So,
hackers would Smurf hundreds of "syn"s to a server.  The server would get so
busy handling false "syn"s that it would never really have enough time to
handle real requests - thus, effectively shutting down the server or more
importantly, it gets denied the ability to communicate its services.

In recent years, patches and software developers increased the buffer size
that handled the syns into the thousands, and then they started creating
individual buffers for specific sockets on servers.  Typical services that
always needed to be running were ports: 23, 25, 69, 80, 110 (probably a few
others) - those ports received their own buffers that could handle thousands
per second while all other ports shared the one main buffer.

And to be honest, I don't know what has been done over the last year or two
to combat SYN attacks.  I do know though, years ago, the Principal Engineer
for MCI wrote a program that used the OSPF Spanning tree algorithm to
back-track smurf attacks.  But it only worked on an ATM backbone because ATM
has the ability, at Layer 2, to check sourcing of incoming packets via PVCs.
The program would start at the Victims router and then login into every
router that connected directly to that one router.  The program would find
the next router traffic was coming through, then login to that router and
perform the same process until eventually, the program reached the source
router.  The source router could be a edge router talking to another
backbone (like Sprint, UUNET, BBN Planet, ANS, etc) or the source router
could be a router that connected to a smaller downstream Tier 2 provider
(regional ISPs) OR the router could be a directly connected customer.  The
only power MCI had was over its directly connected customers and then they
would shut down that customers link until that customer found who the
internal user was that was responsible for the attack.

Anyway, as you read in earlier responses to this thread, there are all new
kinds of DoS attacks these days.  The key to avoid being attacked is: don't
piss anyone off, don't be a mega company with mega dollars, never claim your
site is hack-proof free, don't try to impress the world, don't release
shitty software - oh yeah, and don't have any computers on the internet.

-R

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 17 21:42:49 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 18 Apr 2002 08:42:49 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] CGI arguments passing (newbee question)
In-Reply-To: Message from "E. Egberts" <egbert@familie-egberts.tk>
 of "Wed, 17 Apr 2002 13:56:24 +0200." <NGBBJAFHALILDOAFEDNAEEDJCAAA.egbert@familie-egberts.tk>
Message-ID: <200204172042.IAA17672@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NGBBJAFHALILDOAFEDNAEEDJCAAA.egbert@familie-egberts.tk>, "E. Egberts" writes:
>I'm trying to implement a couple of Perl scripts which expect their
>arguments in the $ARGV array. Can I configure the Xitami web server (version
>2.4d9) such that arguments are passed through this array in stead of the CGI
>envirionment variable QUERY_STRING?

Set [CGI] passargs=1.  It's set to 0 by default, because there are
security risks in passing anything that comes in the query string on the
command line (eg, on some OS certain arguments can be used to run
another command).  Xitami tries to defend against some of the more
obvious ones, but by no means are we certain that it's secure.

If you don't want to set that option, I'd suggest either a wrapper
program to pull query string apart, check the arguments, and then run
the other program; or use a different CGI script that parses
QUERY_STRING as per the CGI spec.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

$sIPFilter        =3D '';
$sHostFilter      =3D '';
$sCounterFilter   =3D '';
$bAutoCreate      =3D 0;

{
  local( $__COUNTER_DAT ) =3D 'livecntr.dat';

  print "Content-type: text/plain\nPragma: no-cache\nCache-control: =
no-cache\nExpires: Mon, 28 Apr 1997 00:01:00 -0500\n\n";


  if( $ARGV[0] )
  {
    local( $nCount ) =3D 0;
    local( $Temp );

    if( '' ne $ARGV[4] )
    {
      $ENV{'HTTP_REFERER'} =3D $ARGV[4];
    }

    if( $ARGV[1] && ( '0' ne $ARGV[1] ) )
    {
      $__COUNTER_DAT =3D $ARGV[1] . '.lcd';
    }

    if( -w "$__COUNTER_DAT" )
    {
      local( $bInc ) =3D 0;

      if( open( F, "+<$__COUNTER_DAT" ) )
      {
        #flock( F, 2 );
        seek( F, 0, 0 );

        ( $Temp, $nCount ) =3D split( /\s/, <F> );

        if( 'i' eq $ARGV[0] )
        {
          local( $bFiltersOk ) =3D 1;

          if( $sURLFilter && ( lc( $ENV{'HTTP_REFERER'} ) !~ $sURLFilter =
) )
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }
          if( $bFiltersOk     &&
              $sIPFilter      && ( $ENV{'REMOTE_ADDR'} =3D~ $sIPFilter ) =
)
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }
          if( $bFiltersOk     &&
              $sHostFilter    && ( $ENV{'REMOTE_HOST'} =3D~ $sHostFilter =
) )
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }
          if( $bFiltersOk     &&
              $sCounterFilter && ( $__COUNTER_DAT =3D~ $sCounterFilter ) =
)
          {
            $bFiltersOk =3D 0;
          }

          if( $bFiltersOk )
          {
            seek( F, 0, 0 );

            ++$nCount;

            print F "Total: $nCount\n";

            $bInc =3D 1;
          }
        }

        #flock( F, 8 );
        close( F );
      }

    }
    elsif( $bAutoCreate )=20
    {
      if( ( !( -e "$__COUNTER_DAT" ) ) && open( F, ">$__COUNTER_DAT" ) )
      {
        print F "Total: 0\n";
        close( F );
      }
    }

    print "c0=3D$nCount\n";
    if( 'v' eq $ARGV[0] )
    {
      print "vr=3D99AX\n";
    }
  }

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 17 22:29:47 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 18 Apr 2002 09:29:47 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] W2K Xitami 2.4d9 crash
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jan de Lint" <jg.de.lint@hccnet.nl>
 of "Wed, 17 Apr 2002 22:43:43 +0200." <01c001c1e650$95c173e0$0200a8c0@mine2>
Message-ID: <200204172129.JAA18404@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <01c001c1e650$95c173e0$0200a8c0@mine2>, "Jan de Lint" writes:
>Would I have more luck (stability) with 2.5b5 which I abandoned because XML
>is/was not handled naturally?

.xml files in the default Xitami 2.5b5 configuration are handled by GSL
scripts.  If you don't want this, you can edit the xitami.cfg file, and
remove the [Wsx] .xml mapping.  (Unfortunately you can't override it in
the defaults.cfg file.)

As for stability issues, 2.4d9 is more likely to be stable than the
2.5b5 beta.  However both do have issues with "dying" from time to time,
unfortunately.

If anyone finds a repeatable pattern to the dying (eg, do this, and then
it dies, every time I do that) then please let us know.  Unfortunately
"it just died" isn't very useful for trying to figure out what is causing
the problem.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 17 22:54:41 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 18 Apr 2002 09:54:41 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] W2K Xitami 2.4d9 crash
In-Reply-To: Message from "Brad Smith" <mata@matatech.tzo.com>
 of "Wed, 17 Apr 2002 17:32:54 -0400." <3CBDB1C6.24094.229BAEA1@localhost>
Message-ID: <200204172154.JAA18897@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3CBDB1C6.24094.229BAEA1@localhost>, "Brad Smith" writes:
>In lieu of an explanation, if someone can guide me to a way I can create 
>a simple service listener, I could deal with option.  In other words, a little 
>app that listens to Xitami, checking to see if it is still running, and, 
>if not, restarts it.  

You don't want to "listen" to Xitami; you want to "check up" on Xitami.
What I do with some servers I monitor is have a special test URL (eg, a
HTML page with some recognisable text on it), and then have a small perl
program (eg, using LWP) check that URL from time to time.  If it doesn't
get the "right" response, then it restarts Xitami (or whatever is being
monitored).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 17 23:31:34 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (M. Jason Smiley)
Date: Wed, 17 Apr 2002 18:31:34 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] W2K Xitami 2.4d9 crash
References: <200204172154.JAA18897@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <038b01c1e65f$a20458c0$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>

we have something like that. we just send request to specific ports and see
if a response come back (try telneting to port 25 of a mail server or port
80 of a web server). we do this for business purposes..... but i've added my
own to test my web / mail / camera servers at home  ;-)

as for restarting the apps - that's another application. our stuff is
complex enough that it needs to be researched and fixed by a person. but a
web or mail server should be pretty simple to restart. i have a batch job
running every night for backups. i also restarts mail servers, dns, etc.

any errors are sent to email or pagers.

simple testing isn't that difficult to develop. ewen's post is another good
example of a way to do this.

>>In lieu of an explanation, if someone can guide me to a way I can create 
>>a simple service listener, I could deal with option.  In other words, a little 
>>app that listens to Xitami, checking to see if it is still running, and, 
>>if not, restarts it.  
>
>You don't want to "listen" to Xitami; you want to "check up" on Xitami.
>What I do with some servers I monitor is have a special test URL (eg, a
>HTML page with some recognisable text on it), and then have a small perl
>program (eg, using LWP) check that URL from time to time.  If it doesn't
>get the "right" response, then it restarts Xitami (or whatever is being

Or you start it from a simple script that runs 'forever'. On OS/2 it looks like: 

[runxitami.cmd]

/* */
Do Forever
'Xitami.exe'
end
exit

Couldn't be much simpler. And reactivates instantly ;-)

>Ewen

Joachim

-----Oorspronkelijk bericht-----
Van: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]Namens Ewen McNeill
Verzonden: woensdag 17 april 2002 22:43
Aan: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Onderwerp: Re: [Xitami] CGI arguments passing (newbee question)


In message <NGBBJAFHALILDOAFEDNAEEDJCAAA.egbert@familie-egberts.tk>, "E.
Egberts" writes:
>I'm trying to implement a couple of Perl scripts which expect their
>arguments in the $ARGV array. Can I configure the Xitami web server
(version
>2.4d9) such that arguments are passed through this array in stead of the
CGI
>envirionment variable QUERY_STRING?

Set [CGI] passargs=1.  It's set to 0 by default, because there are
security risks in passing anything that comes in the query string on the
command line (eg, on some OS certain arguments can be used to run
another command).  Xitami tries to defend against some of the more
obvious ones, but by no means are we certain that it's secure.

If you don't want to set that option, I'd suggest either a wrapper
program to pull query string apart, check the arguments, and then run
the other program; or use a different CGI script that parses
QUERY_STRING as per the CGI spec.

Ewen

--
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Content-Type: text/plain;

Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

I was able to get Virtual Hosts working with Xitami 2.4d9 production
release.

Since I have upgraded to Xitami 2.5b5 beta release, I have been unable to
get Virtual Hosts working.

Let me know which version you have and I might be able to help you out
further.

It's a pretty straight forward process:
    Register the Domain with a registrar to be used as the Vhost DNS name
    Give the Vhost a name
    Type in your Vhost DNS name
    Point to the dir where the files are
    Click Create
    Then go into the Vhost configuration to tweak the settings, such as the
default html page, error logs, security, etc.
    Restart Xitami
    Should work

  ----- Original Message ----- 
  From: Jonathan D. Warren 
  To: xitami@lists.xitami.org 
  Sent: Thursday, April 18, 2002 4:55 PM
  Subject: RE: [Xitami] virtual hosting


  I was able to get Virtual Hosts working with Xitami 2.4d9 production release.

  Since I have upgraded to Xitami 2.5b5 beta release, I have been unable to get Virtual Hosts working.

  Let me know which version you have and I might be able to help you out further.

  It's a pretty straight forward process:
      Register the Domain with a registrar to be used as the Vhost DNS name
      Give the Vhost a name
      Type in your Vhost DNS name
      Point to the dir where the files are
      Click Create
      Then go into the Vhost configuration to tweak the settings, such as the default html page, error logs, security, etc.
      Restart Xitami
      Should work

  From: Jonathan D. Warren 
  To: xitami@lists.xitami.org 
  Sent: Thursday, April 18, 2002 4:55 PM
  Subject: RE: [Xitami] virtual hosting


  I was able to get Virtual Hosts working with Xitami 2.4d9 production release.

  Since I have upgraded to Xitami 2.5b5 beta release, I have been unable to get Virtual Hosts working.

  Let me know which version you have and I might be able to help you out further.

  It's a pretty straight forward process:
      Register the Domain with a registrar to be used as the Vhost DNS name
      Give the Vhost a name
      Type in your Vhost DNS name
      Point to the dir where the files are
      Click Create
      Then go into the Vhost configuration to tweak the settings, such as the default html page, error logs, security, etc.
      Restart Xitami
      Should work

I am trying to set up FTP users for one of my virtual domains.  It is =
working for FTPing via a shell, but if I use the browser (ie: =
ftp://www.domain.com) it doesn't ask for a login and then it redirects =
me to the servers default domain FTP directory.

there are three settings for FTP stuff for each virtual host:
    - ftp root=20
    - ftp users config
    - ftp Directory access

Could someone help me understand the path(s) involved and which settings =
override other settings.  I can config a users default login directory =
to be: /xitami/domain/webpages/ftp  but then I can set the directory =
access to be /xitami/domain and use the same user login that I used in =
the previous config.  What takes precedence?

thanx
-R

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr 19 18:23:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gunnar Swan)
Date: Fri, 19 Apr 2002 10:23:39 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Systrem Tray Icon under NT?
Message-ID: <200204191733.TAA19126@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

Guess what. It's won't start automatically.  If NT boots up, there is
no default 'account'. So Xitami won't run until you log into the console.

Check out www.basta.com. Look at "AppToService"

4/18/02 6:18:02 PM, "Hilmar" <hilmar_koerner@hotmail.com> wrote:

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr 19 20:15:28 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (M. Jason Smiley)
Date: Fri, 19 Apr 2002 15:15:28 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Systrem Tray Icon under NT?
References: <200204191733.TAA19126@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <058201c1e7d6$91afa6f0$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>

you can modify the registry on winnt and w2k to automatically log a user in
on bootup.

i currently do this on my home w2k server box that runs my home web server.
for obvious security reasons it's not a great idea in some environments...
but for home use it's fine.

here are instructions if you want to do this...
http://support.microsoft.com/search/preview.aspx?scid=kb;en-us;Q97597

> Check out www.basta.com. Look at "AppToService"
