From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Apr 20 00:12:04 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gregory Hart)
Date: Fri, 19 Apr 2002 16:12:04 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] ftp issues
References: <091301c1e77e$4cd33450$030000c0@Master>
Message-ID: <001601c1e7f7$a072c8e0$0200a8c0@GregoryHart>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0013_01C1E7BC.F268B1E0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

To me, it sounds like you're allowing anonymous ftp connections. You can =
set up ftp users in ftpusers.aut, or by pressing Define... next to User =
configuration file under FTP. Web Browsers by default try anonymous ftp =
first. You can try ftp://admin@domain.com and that should tell the =
browser to use the name admin and then it should ask for a password.
-Greg

----- Original Message -----=20
From: Russel Olinger=20
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org=20
Sent: Friday, April 19, 2002 1:43 AM
Subject: [Xitami] ftp issues


I am trying to set up FTP users for one of my virtual domains.  It is =
working for FTPing via a shell, but if I use the browser (ie: =
ftp://www.domain.com) it doesn't ask for a login and then it redirects =
me to the servers default domain FTP directory.

there are three settings for FTP stuff for each virtual host:
    - ftp root=20
    - ftp users config
    - ftp Directory access

Could someone help me understand the path(s) involved and which settings =
override other settings.  I can config a users default login directory =
to be: /xitami/domain/webpages/ftp  but then I can set the directory =
access to be /xitami/domain and use the same user login that I used in =
the previous config.  What takes precedence?

thanx
-R

	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Do you have the content-type line in your header? I know Xitami doesn't =
require it, but it couldn't hurt. Just put one of the lines into your =
script if you don't have it:
print "Content-Type: text/html\n\n";
print "Content-Type: text/plain\n\n";
-Greg

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Apr 20 01:53:02 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 20 Apr 2002 12:53:02 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] configuration issue - newbie question
In-Reply-To: Message from "E. Egberts" <egbert@familie-egberts.tk>
 of "Sat, 20 Apr 2002 01:29:18 +0200." <NGBBJAFHALILDOAFEDNAEEECCAAA.egbert@familie-egberts.tk>
Message-ID: <200204200053.MAA01663@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NGBBJAFHALILDOAFEDNAEEECCAAA.egbert@familie-egberts.tk>, "E. Egberts" writes:
>I have setup a small Perl script containing some simple print statements for
>testing purposes. When I execute the script, the browser prompts to download
>a file. This file contains the expected output but I want it to be printed
>in the browser!. Which Xitami configuration parameter (if any) controls this
>output behavior?

Is the script in your CGI-BIN directory?  Does it start with #! /usr/bin/perl
or similar?

Only "executable looking" scripts in your cgi-bin directory will be
executed; the rest will be offered to the browser "as is".

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

In message <NGBBJAFHALILDOAFEDNAEEECCAAA.egbert@familie-egberts.tk>, "E.
Egberts" writes:
>I have setup a small Perl script containing some simple print statements
for
>testing purposes. When I execute the script, the browser prompts to
download
>a file. This file contains the expected output but I want it to be printed
>in the browser!. Which Xitami configuration parameter (if any) controls
this
>output behavior?

Is the script in your CGI-BIN directory?  Does it start with #!
/usr/bin/perl
or similar?

Only "executable looking" scripts in your cgi-bin directory will be
executed; the rest will be offered to the browser "as is".

Then make sure you output a Content-Type: header that is one that the
browser will understand is to be displayed.  text/html or text/plain are
common ones to use.  Otherwise the _browser_ will decide it needs to
save the file.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 22 02:37:48 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jonathan D. Warren)
Date: Sun, 21 Apr 2002 21:37:48 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] virtual hosting
In-Reply-To: <CGEKJMNPHLPPMHMJGJPBGEHHCDAA.lists@myhumbleabode.com>
Message-ID: <CGEKJMNPHLPPMHMJGJPBMEHICDAA.lists@myhumbleabode.com>

Well, after adding tons of debug statements, I finally tracked down the bug.

Here's the info, for those of you that are able to compile the source.

In file "src\smt\smthttp.c", in the function vhost_new(), around line 546
the if logic below is reversed.

orig code:

    /*  Determine rootdir and cgidir for virtual host
*/
    /*  If command-line option is not the default, it takes precedence
*/
    if (streq (rootdir, DEFAULT ("server:webpages")))
        v_rootdir = VCONFIG ("server:webpages");
    else
        v_rootdir = rootdir;

fixed code:

    /*  Determine rootdir and cgidir for virtual host
*/
    /*  If command-line option is not the default, it takes precedence
*/
    if (!streq (rootdir, DEFAULT ("server:webpages")))
        v_rootdir = VCONFIG ("server:webpages");
    else
        v_rootdir = rootdir;

alternate fix:

    /*  Determine rootdir and cgidir for virtual host
*/
    /*  If command-line option is not the default, it takes precedence
*/
    if (streq (rootdir, DEFAULT ("server:webpages")))
        v_rootdir = rootdir;
    else
        v_rootdir = VCONFIG ("server:webpages");

Van: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org

Verzonden: maandag 22 april 2002 3:38
Aan: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Onderwerp: RE: [Xitami] virtual hosting


Well, after adding tons of debug statements, I finally tracked down the bug.

Here's the info, for those of you that are able to compile the source.

In file "src\smt\smthttp.c", in the function vhost_new(), around line 546
the if logic below is reversed.

orig code:

    /*  Determine rootdir and cgidir for virtual host
*/
    /*  If command-line option is not the default, it takes precedence
*/
    if (streq (rootdir, DEFAULT ("server:webpages")))
        v_rootdir = VCONFIG ("server:webpages");
    else
        v_rootdir = rootdir;

fixed code:

    /*  Determine rootdir and cgidir for virtual host
*/
    /*  If command-line option is not the default, it takes precedence
*/
    if (!streq (rootdir, DEFAULT ("server:webpages")))
        v_rootdir = VCONFIG ("server:webpages");
    else
        v_rootdir = rootdir;

alternate fix:

    /*  Determine rootdir and cgidir for virtual host
*/
    /*  If command-line option is not the default, it takes precedence
*/
    if (streq (rootdir, DEFAULT ("server:webpages")))
        v_rootdir = rootdir;
    else
        v_rootdir = VCONFIG ("server:webpages");

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 22 18:14:23 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Kevin Brogan)
Date: Mon, 22 Apr 2002 10:14:23 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] i fixed the bug
Message-ID: <001a01c1ea21$260114f0$23a24118@kevin>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

--Boundary_(ID_uQHXdqagqBNGjLnlJmjfoA)
Content-type: text/plain; charset=iso-8859-1
Content-transfer-encoding: 7BIT

Looking through the xitami config files, i see an option called "cache default pages." Since I'm having trouble with the default pages I think, what the hey, and I uncheck the option. Voila, I get the correct index page now.

--Boundary_(ID_uQHXdqagqBNGjLnlJmjfoA)
Content-type: text/html; charset=iso-8859-1
Content-transfer-encoding: 7BIT

<!DOCTYPE HTML PUBLIC "-//W3C//DTD HTML 4.0 Transitional//EN">
<HTML><HEAD>
<META http-equiv=Content-Type content="text/html; charset=iso-8859-1">
<META content="MSHTML 6.00.2715.400" name=GENERATOR>
<STYLE></STYLE>
</HEAD>
<BODY bgColor=#ffffff>
<DIV><FONT face=Arial size=2>Looking through the xitami config files, i see an

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 22 21:03:52 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 23 Apr 2002 08:03:52 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] virtual host alias wilcards
In-Reply-To: Message from Kevin Brogan <dragonscales@saltspring.com>
 of "Mon, 22 Apr 2002 09:52:34 MST." <000f01c1ea1e$1a3e6620$23a24118@kevin>
Message-ID: <200204222003.IAA11619@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <000f01c1ea1e$1a3e6620$23a24118@kevin>, Kevin Brogan writes:
>for example, right now, i need to define two virtual hosts. one for http://mydo
>main.com and another for http://www.mydomain.com
>It it possible to instead, define a virtual host as http://*.mydomain.com?

No, there's no wildcard mechanism (other than making it he default
host).  You can, however, point multiple domain names at the same
virtual host config file, eg.

[Virtual-Hosts]
  mydomain.com=mydomain.cfg
  www.mydomain.com=mydomain.cfg

which can save some time in setting things up.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Apr 23 01:26:46 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gregory Hart)
Date: Mon, 22 Apr 2002 17:26:46 -0700
Subject: Fw: [Xitami] How to set up Aliases
Message-ID: <003901c1ea5d$8e87b100$0200a8c0@GregoryHart>

Aliases is on the menu for the web browser admin screen. Just click Configuration and then on Aliases, which is on the right side.
Alias goes to Alias and Directory goes to Points to path. You should already have read access. To setup execute, just point the
cgi-bin to your alias or higher, like your web page directory.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Apr 23 20:17:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 23 Apr 2002 15:17:39 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] PHP 4.0.2+ $PHP_SELF empty
In-Reply-To: <5.1.0.14.2.20020422235204.01c327c0@mail.earthlink.net>
References: <5.1.0.14.2.20020422235204.01c327c0@mail.earthlink.net>
Message-ID: <741432953398.20020423151739@rci.rutgers.edu>

> $PHP_SELF is set, but empty!

> $SCRIPT_NAME works just the same.  Give that a try.

> a pain to change code.

Don't change the code.

Make a BAT file called PHP-fix.BAT

 @echo off
 set  $PHP_SELF=$SCRIPT_NAME
 c:\php\bin\php.exe %1 %2 %3 %4 %5

(I may have screwed-up the syntax, but you'll figure it out.)

Tell Xitami to send PHP file to PHP-fix.BAT

 -PRR


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Apr 23 21:24:14 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Steve Shervais)
Date: Tue, 23 Apr 2002 13:24:14 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Yet Another VH Problem
Message-ID: <007701c1eb04$d6418820$a419bb92@ewu.edu>

I am running a student webserver under Xitami v2.5b4 on an old Win95 box.
Works fine.

Recently, I tried setting up virtual hosts (using the wizard, mostly) for
different teams, and trying to give each team their own logs, so they can
see what their errors look like.  Xitami created the logs for me
(teamXX.log, teamXXerr.log), and in the correct directory.  However, none of
the logs has any entries -- all the information is going into the default
logs under C:\Xitami.  This seems to be because Xitami is ignoring the VH
entries and using the defaults.  Here are the contents of defaults.cfg, a
team config file, and an extract from debug.

In defaults.cfg I have:
[Virtual-hosts]
    Eaglebay.ewu.edu/teamXX = "teamXX.cfg"
----------------------------------------------
In teamXX.cfg I have:
#*END

[Accesslog]
    Filename = "C:/Xitami/webpages/teamXX/logs/teamXX.log"
    enabled=1

[Errorlog]
    Filename = "C:/Xitami/webpages/teamXX/logs/teamXXErr.log"
    enabled=1

[Ftp]
    Root = "C:/Xitami/webpages/teamXX"

[Server]
    Defaults="defaults.cfg"
    Cgi-bin = "C:/Xitami/webpages/teamXX/cgi-bin"
    Webpages = "C:/Xitami/webpages/teamXX"
    Hostname="eaglebay.ewu.edu"
----------------------------------------------
In debug I see:
2002/04/23 13:12:06: Looking for VH using Host value: eaglebay.ewu.edu
2002/04/23 13:12:06:  - looking for VH using IP address: 146.187.25.27
2002/04/23 13:12:06: - using default virtual host values

So, any obvious errors? Any recommendations?

Regards,
Steve Shervais

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Apr 24 01:07:23 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gregory Hart)
Date: Tue, 23 Apr 2002 17:07:23 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Yet Another VH Problem
References: <007701c1eb04$d6418820$a419bb92@ewu.edu>
Message-ID: <004901c1eb24$0349c200$0200a8c0@GregoryHart>

The virual host is for domain names, like freastro.net or files.freastro.net. It will not work for directories in a domain, like
freastro.net/path1 or files.freastro.net/path2.
-Greg

>2002/04/23 13:12:06: Looking for VH using Host value: eaglebay.ewu.edu

>2002/04/23 13:12:06: - using default virtual host values

For some reason it is not matching your virtual hosts -- and hence is
returning the "default" webpages, and hence logging in the default logs.

You'll need to make sure that the defaults.cfg file points at your
virtual hosts with entries like:

[virtual-host]
  domainname=config

and also that the domain name is being passed in with a HTTP/1.1 Host:
header (which it appears to be from the snippet that you list).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

References: <DAECIFPNFLGIHMJEOGHMEEMBCBAA.spantazi@uvic.ca>

Xitami protects its logs from being used from other programs, just like using flock in perl. I think what's happening is that it's
not unprotecting them before it renames them. This could possibly be a bug. You could try having it append to another file or move
it instead of renaming it.
-Greg

Question on Attachments to E-mail:

 

Used Net::SMTP from ActiveState to set up sub to send mail.
This 
subroutine works correctly, but doesn't provide for
file attachments. Listed 
SMTP.pm and found entry points
for mail, to, data, and quit, but none for 
attach.

 

Do I need to use another module or can Net::SMTP be 
used?
 
Also, is there a module available for faxing files?

 

Listed below is the sub I'm using.

 

sub send_mail
{ my ($to, $from, $subject, @body, $attach)=@_;
  
use Net::SMTP;

 

  my $relay = "smtp.earthlink.net";
  my $smtp  = 
Net::SMTP- new($relay);
  die "Open of mail failed" if (! defined 
$smtp);
  print "Open of mail OK", " BR ";

 

  print "Mail beg", " BR ";
  
$smtp- mail($from);
  $smtp- to($to);
  
$smtp- data();
  $smtp- datasend("To: $to\n");
  
$smtp- datasend("From: $from\n");
  $smtp- datasend("Subject: 
$subject\n");
  $smtp- datasend("\n");
  
foreach(@body)
  {
    
$smtp- datasend("$_\n");
  }
  
$smtp- dataend("\n");
  $smtp- quit;
}

I created a simple perl script that would allow me to stream real player files using the free player. The script is:

#!/usr/local/bin/perl

$forminfo = $ENV{'QUERY_STRING'};
$forminfo =~ s/%([0-9a-fA-F][0-9a-fA-F])/pack("C", hex($1))/eg;

print "Content-type: application/vnd.rn-realmedia\n\n";
print "$forminfo\n";

You could also use the object tag in HTML and put it into a web page that way. If you could get me more information on specifically
what type of video file it is and if you want to display it in a different program or on a web page, I'd be able to help you more.
-Greg

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr 26 01:35:43 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gregory Hart)
Date: Thu, 25 Apr 2002 17:35:43 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] [Xitami]Attachments to E-mail?
References: <4120024425171934610@earthlink.net>
Message-ID: <001901c1ecba$4dda2a20$0200a8c0@GregoryHart>

I found this at http://www-old.ics.uci.edu/pub/websoft/libwww-perl/archive/1999h1/0053.html. The message is below:

You might want to check out MIME::Entity and company, specifically, the
build, attach, print, and stringify methods.

For example (from MIME::Entity documentation):

my $msg = MIME::Entity->build(
 From     => 'me@myhost.com',
 To       => 'you@yourhost.com',
 Subject  => "Hello, nurse!",
 Data     => [
  'body text line 1',
  'body text line 2',
  'body text line 3'
 ]
);
$msg->attach(
 Path => $my_file_to_attach,
 Type => $my_files_mime_type,
 Encoding => '-SUGGEST'
);
# set up SMTP recipient, sender here
$smtp->datasend($msg->stringify);

# or possibly $msg->print $smtp (I haven't tried this)

So you just use $smtp->datasend once in this case instead of multiple times. Since you have mutliple lines of data, you should be
able to use Data => @body. Hope that works.
-Greg

----- Original Message -----
From:
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Sent: Thursday, April 25, 2002 10:19 AM
Subject: [Xitami] [Xitami]Attachments to E-mail?



Question on Attachments to E-mail:

Used Net::SMTP from ActiveState to set up sub to send mail.
This subroutine works correctly, but doesn't provide for
file attachments. Listed SMTP.pm and found entry points
for mail, to, data, and quit, but none for attach.

Do I need to use another module or can Net::SMTP be used?

Also, is there a module available for faxing files?

Listed below is the sub I'm using.

sub send_mail
{ my ($to, $from, $subject, @body, $attach)=@_;
  use Net::SMTP;

  my $relay = "smtp.earthlink.net";
  my $smtp  = Net::SMTP->new($relay);
  die "Open of mail failed" if (! defined $smtp);
  print "Open of mail OK", "<BR>";

  print "Mail beg", "<BR>";
  $smtp->mail($from);
  $smtp->to($to);
  $smtp->data();
  $smtp->datasend("To: $to\n");
  $smtp->datasend("From: $from\n");
  $smtp->datasend("Subject: $subject\n");
  $smtp->datasend("\n");
  foreach(@body)
  {
    $smtp->datasend("$_\n");
  }
  $smtp->dataend("\n");
  $smtp->quit;
}

Hi,

If you are going to stream QuickTime videos there is a free, open source
streaming server called Darwin available on Apple
http://www.apple.com/quicktime/products/qtss/
I remember that it needs a perl engine to run at the same time but other
than this, the only thing you need to worry is your streaming server
bandwidth. I think you don't even need xitami to run the streaming server,
it can be a totally separate, machine. Of course you need a webserver to
store the webpages with the streaming links or embeds.

Good luck
Stefan

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr 26 02:15:22 2002

I quickly tested it and this should work:

#!/usr/local/bin/perl

$forminfo = $ENV{'QUERY_STRING'};
$forminfo =~ s/%([0-9a-fA-F][0-9a-fA-F])/pack("C", hex($1))/eg;

print "Content-type: audio/mpeg\n\n";
print "$forminfo\n";

Just call the script like this: script.pl?http://www.domain.com/audio_file.mp3. If you want a video file, just change the content
type to video/mpeg.
-Greg

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Apr 26 02:52:26 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gregory Hart)
Date: Thu, 25 Apr 2002 18:52:26 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Streaming Video
References: <3CC86BC8.25430.21B7CC1@localhost> <001101c1ecbf$d7d73b00$0200a8c0@GregoryHart>
Message-ID: <002101c1ecc5$054f9aa0$0200a8c0@GregoryHart>

If you don't have perl, and you have a file, for example, video.mpv, you could create another file, stream.mpv, and put
http://www.domain.com/video.mpv in it. This is basically what the perl script does. The video.mpv is the file that you want to
steam. When someone clicks on stream.mpv, Xitami automatically sends the content type, video/mpeg, and when the media player opens,
it looks at http://www.domain.com/video.mpv and redirects to that file. Hope this helps for those without perl.
-Greg

------=_NextPart_000_0006_01C1EE29.70587640
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Open your web browser, go to http://localhost/admin, click on =
configuration, and then change the cgi-bin directory to your webpage =
directory, or a directory in your webpage directory.
-Greg

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr 28 05:07:43 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gregory Hart)
Date: Sat, 27 Apr 2002 21:07:43 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] cgi-bin in webpage folder
References: <000a01c1ee5f$2fc618e0$85c907c4@h8s2o0> <000901c1ee64$1db31360$0200a8c0@GregoryHart> <003401c1ee67$f7decae0$85c907c4@h8s2o0>

------=_NextPart_000_0006_01C1EE2F.92A8E3A0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

It depends on what you mean by a whole lot of sites. If you are just =
using one configuration, but you want many directories that you want to =
have cgi access, you just put the cgi-bin directory to your webpage =
directory. If you have virtual hosts, instead of clicking on =
configuration, you need to click on virtual hosts, then on the =
configuration that you want to change, and then you can change the =
cgi-bin directory. If you mean something different, just email me. Hope =
that helps!
-Greg

----- Original Message -----=20
From: A Message from Africa=20
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org=20
Sent: Saturday, April 27, 2002 8:51 PM

  Subject: Re: [Xitami] cgi-bin in webpage folder

directory, or a directory in your webpage directory.
  -Greg

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr 28 21:44:33 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gregory Hart)
Date: Sun, 28 Apr 2002 13:44:33 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] cgi-bin in webpage folder
References: <000a01c1ee5f$2fc618e0$85c907c4@h8s2o0> <000901c1ee64$1db31360$0200a8c0@GregoryHart> <003401c1ee67$f7decae0$85c907c4@h8s2o0> <000901c1ee6a$418d2e00$0200a8c0@GregoryHart> <003f01c1ee75$2054d7a0$85c907c4@h8s2o0>

------=_NextPart_000_0006_01C1EEBA.D435ADE0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Just go into the 'Configuration' menu from http://localhost/admin, and =
then it should show a page with many text boxes. The first three are the =
ones that you want to focus on. The first one called 'Main HTML =
directory' is your webpage directory. Change the one called 'Main CGI =
directory' to the 'Main HTML directory'. Next, change the 'CGI URLs =
start with' to /. Finally, press Save at the top left and you'll be =
brought to the main menu. The last step is to press Restart in the top =
right corner. It should say 'Server is restarting...' and then you can =
start using your cgi files in your webpage directory, or any sub-folders =
in it, once you see that message.

If it still doesn't work, try right-clicking on Xitami and press =
terminate. Then you need to start Xitami again.

I hope that works for you! Email me again if still have problems.
-Greg

  ----- Original Message -----=20
  From: Gregory Hart=20
  To: xitami@lists.xitami.org=20
  Sent: Sunday, April 28, 2002 6:07 AM
  Subject: Re: [Xitami] cgi-bin in webpage folder


  It depends on what you mean by a whole lot of sites. If you are just =
using one configuration, but you want many directories that you want to =
have cgi access, you just put the cgi-bin directory to your webpage =
directory. If you have virtual hosts, instead of clicking on =
configuration, you need to click on virtual hosts, then on the =
configuration that you want to change, and then you can change the =
cgi-bin directory. If you mean something different, just email me. Hope =
that helps!
  -Greg

    Open your web browser, go to http://localhost/admin, click on =
configuration, and then change the cgi-bin directory to your webpage =
directory, or a directory in your webpage directory.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 29 01:10:45 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Chris Olson)
Date: Sun, 28 Apr 2002 19:10:45 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami2.4d9 and PHP4
Message-ID: <3CCC8F85.92421180@astcomm.net>

I tested Xitami for about a year and a half, then finally gave up on it and
went back to Apache.  I'm back testing it again, trying to run a php4 driven
MySQL database application to see if it will reduce CPU/memory load over
what Apache uses.  The server is running on a twin Pentium-Pro, powered by
Debian Linux/2.2.19 kernel, and 512MB RAM.  Apache version is 1.3.24 with
PHP4.4.1 as loadable module for Apache, and using the php4-mysql module to
drive the database.  All applications installed with Debian debs from the
woody distro.

Question:
Can Xitami be used with the PHP module for Apache, or do I have to compile a
seperate PHP app on the server?  If I need the seperate PHP app, I'll
compile it and drop it in.

Question:
It's been awhile, but if I remember correctly, to enable parsing of PHP you
have to add a line for a filter like: .php=/path/to/php4/executable ???

Other observations:
* Xitami *still* doesn't write a PID file on UNIX platforms.  This was one
of my pet peeves with the previous versions as well - it'd be nice to be
able to run Xitami from init.d or tcpserver on UNIX hosts instead of having
to use killall to stop the process and a script to start it when
configurations are changed or virtual domains added or removed.

* The FTP server still won't handle hardly any load at all - I've found I
can't use it for serious FTP work.

* The webbased admin panel still positively rocks - much easier than editing
Apache's config file via ssh, and then reloading the server with
/etc/init.d/apache reload.  But I can't get Xitami's server restart function
to work every time when throwing in a new domain or making other config
changes that require reload of the /usr/local/bin/xitami/defaults.cfg file. 
I've found I still have to ssh to the box, kill xitami, then execute the
start script to fire it back up and force the config file reload.  Others
have this problem?

Regards,
-- 
Chris Olson
System Administrator
AST Communications  http://www.astcomm.net

Subject: [Xitami] Xitami2.4d9 and PHP4
References: <3CCC8F85.92421180@astcomm.net>

Chris Olson wrote: 
> I tested Xitami for about a year and a half, then finally gave up on it and
> went back to Apache.  I'm back testing it again, trying to run a php4 driven
> MySQL database application to see if it will reduce CPU/memory load over
> what Apache uses.  The server is running on a twin Pentium-Pro, powered by
> Debian Linux/2.2.19 kernel, and 512MB RAM.  Apache version is 1.3.24 with
> PHP4.4.1 as loadable module for Apache, and using the php4-mysql module to
> drive the database.  All applications installed with Debian debs from the
> woody distro.

I answered most of my own questions <g>.

I had to compile php4 --with-mysql to work with Xitami and this application
- the php4 module for apache wouldn't work.  The results are somewhat
disappointing.

This was a good time of the evening to test Xitami, as the server is running
under a fairly heavy load.  This is an online message board application
hosted for the GWTA.  This server is running at a constant load of about
11,500 hits per hour this time of the evening.  This would be no problem
with static pages, but this is a totally dynamic php4/mysql database
application which greatly increases CPU and memory load due to parsing
scripts and database calls - the database server is running on the same
machine.

Monitoring processes and performance, using top, shows apache using
approximately 67% of the total memory (both physical and swap) and the CPU's
running an average of 17-21% idle.  Apache isn't using all the CPU power -
quite a bit of it is being used by the mysql daemons, which fork like
apache.  Running 'ps -ef|grep apache' shows an average of 190-200 seperate
httpd processes fairly continuous.  This varies between peaks and valleys of
load, as some of the server processes die off when load goes down, and
apache spawns new ones as load increases.

Xitami is different.  It can handle this application until a peak in the
demand hits.  When load peaks, Xitami requires increasing memory to spawn
new threads, but not as much as apache.  Apache is fairly constantly
requiring 350-400 MB of memory.  The CPU power is another matter.  Xitami is
using it all, and the server slows to a dead crawl when the load peaks.  The
only explanation I can come up with is that the parsing of the php scripting
is not quite as efficient as the way apache is doing it.

Is there a way to optomize php for Xitami?  Or a loadable module similar to
apache's?  Xitami isn't listed in the documentation for the current release
of PHP4.

Regards,
--
Chris Olson
System Administrator
AST Communications  http://www.astcomm.net

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 29 03:56:44 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 29 Apr 2002 14:56:44 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami2.4d9 and PHP4
In-Reply-To: Message from Chris Olson <chris@astcomm.net>
 of "Sun, 28 Apr 2002 21:29:11 EST." <3CCCAFF7.DFAA3DE1@astcomm.net>
Message-ID: <200204290256.OAA02180@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3CCCAFF7.DFAA3DE1@astcomm.net>, Chris Olson writes:
>Chris Olson wrote: 
>Is there a way to optomize php for Xitami?  Or a loadable module similar to
>apache's?  Xitami isn't listed in the documentation for the current release
>of PHP4.

There's no loadable module for PHP for Xitami; in fact as far as I
recall the loadable module is only for Apache, and PHP was originally
written to run only with Apache.  A couple of years back I ran into one
of the authors of PHP at a conference, and we spoke briefly about the
idea of better integration between Xitami and PHP but no one has really
had time investigate it much further.

In the case of PHP and Xitami, the real killer under load is that PHP is 
being run as a CGI (a filter in Xitami is basically a CGI process in
disguise).  The overhead of forking and starting up the CGI process, and
dragging the output back in from the output files gets pretty noticable
when things get busy.  Apache/mod-php avoids all that overhead.

The obvious half way house is to turn PHP into a LRWP process attached
to Xitami, an idea that we played around with briefly some time ago but
never quite got completed.  If someone (who knows how to write C code)
is interested in playing with this idea let me know, and I'll try to
find the source code we'd thrown together.

>From your other message:
>* Xitami *still* doesn't write a PID file on UNIX platforms.  

I actually suspect that it's still the same version of Xitami as you
last noted this problem with.  We haven't noticed the source growing
new functions all by itself... :-)  (Yes, alas, the release versions of
Xitami have hardly changed in two years :-(  Even our internal versions
have changed all that much, although some of the libraries have.)

Contributions of source code to write a PID file much appreciated.  (I'd
find it handy too...)

>* The FTP server still won't handle hardly any load at all - I've found
>  I can't use it for serious FTP work.

This has been fairly widely noted.  We do recommend using another FTP
server if you're doing all that much with FTP.  The one in Xitami is
basically a very lightweight one for when you don't have/want to install
another.  I'd like to make it more robust myself, but simply haven't had
the time.

>But I can't get Xitami's server restart function to work every time 
>when throwing in a new domain or making other config changes that 
>require reload of the /usr/local/bin/xitami/defaults.cfg file. 

A number of people have noted this too.  I suspect there's just not 
quite enough checking of all the files going on.  But it's another
thing that we haven't been able to make enough time to investigate.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Apr 28 23:23:46 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sun, 28 Apr 2002 22:23:46
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami DoS/DDoS (CFM, PHP, Perl, and *ALL* CGIs)...
In-Reply-To: <200204070741.TAA12984@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
References: <Message from "Gregory Hart" <freastro@yahoo.com>
 <002801c1d849$75fe5920$0200a8c0@geh>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020428222346.009f37a8@shininglightpro.com>

I previously e-mailed this list about a problem with 50 simultaneous
connections to CGI scripts under Xitami.  I have since performed additional
testing and have come to the conclusion that CGIs are a fatal source of
DoS/DDoS attacks with the Xitami webserver under Windows (others have
complained about Xitami slowing to a crawl under Linux).  Below are the
steps that I took to come to this conclusion:

1)  I fixed my localhost Distributed Attack Server/Client (DAS/DAC) so that
it didn't crash (really silly problem dealing with attempting to allocate
and write to the same area of memory at the same time).

2)  I fixed many of XiFusion's bugs that people have mentioned since the
release of v2.5.

3)  I re-ran the DAS/DAC.  The same problems arose as before in the logs.
Just a refresher, the log files look like this under a 60 user load:
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:20:49 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 99340
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:25 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist3.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 5
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:25 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist3.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 5
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:26 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 1117
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:26 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 1
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:26 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 1
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 0
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 0
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist3.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 0
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 1

The above sample logs should have been the following:

127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:20:49 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 99340
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:25 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist3.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 5
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:25 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist3.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 5
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:26 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 1117
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:26 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 99340
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:26 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 1117
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 99340
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 1117
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist3.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 5
127.0.0.1 - - [28/Apr/2002:15:28:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.cfm
HTTP/1.1" 200 99340

Obviously, a very serious problem is occurring here.  Sometimes I am
getting zero bytes returned, one byte returned, and the rest of the time
the correct number of bytes returned.

At this point, I whipped out my compiler, Borland's C RTL, and downloaded
the latest stable Xitami source.

4)  Next, I wrote my own function that calls CreateProcess and
WaitForSingleObject to see if either function fails within XiFusion.  The
same problems arose and neither function failed.

5)  I created a file for every single thread started in the DAC to track
exactly what happens with each thread.  The DAC stopped opening files after
47 files were opened.  The problem:  The number of open files had been
exceeded for the application.

Obviously, I only hit a C library limitation, but it dawned on me that
since CreateProcess was not failing and WaitForSingleObject was not
failing, creating the file handle is the only alternative.  Below is a
logical explanation of what is happening inside both Xitami and XiFusion:

1)  A request comes to the Xitami webserver for a CGI-based application
(assume for this example XiFusion is associated with the file extension).
2)  Xitami calls the function process_create() to launch the CGI.
3)  Inside process_create(), the function redirect_io() is called three
times (once for each standard handle).  This creates three file I/O handles
which the CGI is supposed to dump its data into.  However, there is no test
for whether or not the file was opened successfully within redirect_io()
for both std_out and std_err.  If either fails to open,
INVALID_HANDLE_VALUE is returned (which is -1) and the resulting value is
assigned to the STARTUPINFO structure that is submitted to CreateProcess().
4)  XiFusion is then launched via CreateProcess and then the process is
waited on (CreateProcess rarely ever fails (only under low system resources
will it fail) and I have yet to see WaitForSingleObject to fail as well - I
also have set my CGIs to run until they finish).  Note, at this point in
the Xitami code, it fails to detect whether WaitForSingleObject() fails or
not.
5)  XiFusion's underlying Borland C RTL fails to detect whether
GetStdHandle fails.  The value at this point should be INVALID_HANDLE_VALUE
if Xitami failed to create the file handle.  All output data will therefore
fail to be displayed, hence zero bytes returned.
6)  XiFusion itself fails to check to see if its own stdout redirection
fails.  Hence the return of only one byte of data (padding) in some cases
where stdout was successfully created by Xitami.
7)  Only very rarely, will both redirected input and output handles get
created in Xitami and the redirected output handle in XiFusion (Xitami has
a better chance of creating the redirected input handle since it will
Sleep(1000) if it fails to be created).  This explains the occasional
correct number of bytes returned from the server.


MSDN Library demonstrates the correct way to start processes with
redirected input and output:

MSDN Library->Platform SDK->Base Services->DLLs, Processes, and
Threads->Processes and Threads->Using Processes and Threads->Creating a
Child Process with Redirected Input and Output

Unfortunately, most compiler writers use the poor example mentioned in the
CreateProcess() description.

Under normal circumstances this issue will not occur, but under very heavy
CGI usage, the problems will appear frequently (95-99% of the time).
End-users will be unable to get results and their browsers will, in many
cases, appear to hang on a completed webpage (zero bytes returned).
Several people have mentioned that I should make XiFusion a LRWP
application.  Doing this is possible, but a DoS/DDoS can still take place
just as easily (600 simultaneous users instead of 60).  It really does not
matter...the problem is that both Xitami and XiFusion have a major DoS/DDoS
issue that is going to take a while to fix.

Ewen, I have a 'localhost' version of the DAS/DAC ready if you want it for
testing purposes.  I don't want to distribute it to others because of the
implications this particular DoS has.

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

Quite possibly.  ISTR that there are either Javascript or CSS conflicts

if that helps.  That said, config reloading in Xitami has always been a
tiny bit dodgy, particularly where the server is running setuid
something other than root.

  ----- Original Message -----=20

  Just go into the 'Configuration' menu from http://localhost/admin, and =
then it should show a page with many text boxes. The first three are the =
ones that you want to focus on. The first one called 'Main HTML =
directory' is your webpage directory. Change the one called 'Main CGI =
directory' to the 'Main HTML directory'. Next, change the 'CGI URLs =
start with' to /. Finally, press Save at the top left and you'll be =
brought to the main menu. The last step is to press Restart in the top =
right corner. It should say 'Server is restarting...' and then you can =
start using your cgi files in your webpage directory, or any sub-folders =
in it, once you see that message.

  If it still doesn't work, try right-clicking on Xitami and press =
terminate. Then you need to start Xitami again.

  I hope that works for you! Email me again if still have problems.
  -Greg

    It depends on what you mean by a whole lot of sites. If you are just =
using one configuration, but you want many directories that you want to =
have cgi access, you just put the cgi-bin directory to your webpage =
directory. If you have virtual hosts, instead of clicking on =
configuration, you need to click on virtual hosts, then on the =
configuration that you want to change, and then you can change the =
cgi-bin directory. If you mean something different, just email me. Hope =
that helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 29 10:43:02 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Mon, 29 Apr 2002 09:43:02
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami DoS/DDoS (CFM, PHP, Perl, and *ALL*
 CGIs)...
In-Reply-To: <3CCD535D.6060805@freesbee.fr>
References: <Message from "Gregory Hart" <freastro@yahoo.com>
 <002801c1d849$75fe5920$0200a8c0@geh>
 <3.0.6.32.20020428222346.009f37a8@shininglightpro.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020429094302.00a10db0@shininglightpro.com>

At 04:06 PM 4/29/2002 +0200, Francis Turner writeth:
>Very interesting.
>
>I wonder if this explains my persisitant GSL/XML problem(s). Sounds 
>higly plausible.

Could you elaborate on those problems?  I have seen various, related
incidents in the past month or so since this issue arose.  The most recent
one is under Linux with CGIs causing the server to be very unresponsive
under heavy loads.  There was an earlier one with Win98 crashing on a low
memory system and many CGIs opening at once.  You get the idea...

>I suppose I'd better look at the source to fiure out how the XML/GSL 
>stuff differs from an external CGI. It is true that my XML problems have 
>got worse when I use statements like
>.xml from <filename>
>thus requiring more files to be opened at a given moment.

Remember that filters are CGIs in "disguise."  They have somewhat different
properties than CGIs, but are basically the same.

Also, unless you have 50-60 simultaneous users on the system using CGIs,
this problem will go unnoticed.  However, a malicious attacker can easily
cause a DoS/DDoS with a simple tool that just requests CGI-oriented scripts
on the remote server to be executed - the server is quickly brought to its
knees and other users are unable to get webpages (usually the browser
appears to hang when the server replies with zero bytes of data - a flaw in
one of the Windows API calls that the browser has little control over).

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Apr 29 17:21:59 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 29 Apr 2002 12:21:59 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] New version for Xitami
In-Reply-To: <3CCC6531.3060803@ultinet.org>
References: <3CCC6531.3060803@ultinet.org>
Message-ID: <13051224306.20020429122159@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I wanted to know when a new release of Xitami is due..

Maybe never.

Xitami was released as a demo to promote a young programming
company, Imatix. In cross-platform and simplicity of use, it was
ahead of its time. Imatix has been quite successful, not by selling
and supporting Xitami but by selling programming tools and custom
software.

Xitami has been popular, but mostly because it is free. That
generates no income for Imatix, and they are not putting company
resources into it. They apparently have more than enough paid work
to keep them busy. They can't put someone on an Xitami problem for
hours or days, when paying customers are pushing money at them for
custom work.

Xitami is open source, but has not attracted the critical mass of
user support needed to carry on from where Imatix turned to paying
projects. That would be very nice, but I know I can't be of much
help with something as complex as a webserver, and apparently there
are not many others here who have the knowledge and time needed to
improve the product.

Ewen of Imatix, out of the goodness of his heart, and on his own
time, watches this list and has pushed some critical patches out.
But Xitami is still pretty much where it was several years ago. In
fact not counting the stuff added in the 2.5 beta, which was adopted
from other Imatix projects and tossed on top of 2.4, it is really
quite old.

If you want a up-to-date server with ample support, Apache is it.
There are 100 or 1,000 times more users of Apache than Xitami, which
apparently means more than enough skilled programmers to handle
improvements, and a large community of ordinary users to share
knowledge. That ini file in Apache makes my head spin, but it isn't
really all that hard, and Apache's many mature features and quick
patching make it worthwhile.

I'm still on Xitami. My needs are simple and Xitami works for me.
But the day I find something that Xitami just won't do, I'm off to
Apache.

BTW: V-hosts work fine for me with 2.4. Except sometimes the machine
needs to be re-booted to pick up the changes. Since I add a V-host
maybe once in 6 months, and Windows' TCP stack needs a kick every
few months, I don't see it as a problem. For a many-customer ISP,
where V-hosts would be added daily, Xitami probably isn't the best
choice.

 -PRR

this problem will go unnoticed.  However, a malicious attacker can easily
cause a DoS/DDoS with a simple tool that just requests CGI-oriented scripts
on the remote server to be executed - the server is quickly brought to its
knees and other users are unable to get webpages (usually the browser
appears to hang when the server replies with zero bytes of data - a flaw in
one of the Windows API calls that the browser has little control over).

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

The CLF (Common Logfile Format) format is generally considered the standard.

> Also would anyone be able to suggest a better solution than WebTrends for
> Web Stats Reporting that would run better with Xitami?

We use Webalizer on our servers, run from a daily cron job. I can't
remember what their website is right offhand but a google search for
webalizer should get you there. I've been able to process CLF files from
both Xitami and Apache with no problems.

In message <3CCD520B.6040305@freesbee.fr> Francis Turner writes:
> bernd hohmann wrote:
> 
> >sb. compiled a version for windows a week ago, i compiled a
> >version for OS/2 and a patch was in this newsgroup too so a *nix
> >version shouldn't be a real problem.
> >
> Who is sb? and for those of us who can't readily compile a windows 
> version has anyone produced a binary with recent fixes in?

I believe (BICBW) that "sb" is an abbreviation for "somebody".  I see
this abbreviation used in many newsgroups, by German speakers writing in
English.  I cannot remember ever seeing it used by anyone for whom
English is their first language (no, not even by a schoolkid 'sndng
txt msgs 2 hs m8t usng SMS' :-)

One also sees "so" for "someone" as well.  Quite where this usage
originated, I don't know; certainly neither abbreviation is to be found
in any dictionary of the English language.   (To me, "sb" is an
abbreviation USED BY dictionaries, for "substantive", whilst "so" is
sometimes seen in newsgroups, as "SO", for "significant other".)

From: Chris Olson <chris@astcomm.net>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Sunday, April 28, 2002 5:10 PM
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami2.4d9 and PHP4


I tested Xitami for about a year and a half, then finally gave up on it and
went back to Apache.  I'm back testing it again, trying to run a php4 driven
MySQL database application to see if it will reduce CPU/memory load over
what Apache uses.  The server is running on a twin Pentium-Pro, powered by
Debian Linux/2.2.19 kernel, and 512MB RAM.  Apache version is 1.3.24 with
PHP4.4.1 as loadable module for Apache, and using the php4-mysql module to
drive the database.  All applications installed with Debian debs from the
woody distro.

Question:
Can Xitami be used with the PHP module for Apache, or do I have to compile a
seperate PHP app on the server?  If I need the seperate PHP app, I'll
compile it and drop it in.

Question:
It's been awhile, but if I remember correctly, to enable parsing of PHP you
have to add a line for a filter like: .php=/path/to/php4/executable ???

Other observations:
* Xitami *still* doesn't write a PID file on UNIX platforms.  This was one
of my pet peeves with the previous versions as well - it'd be nice to be
able to run Xitami from init.d or tcpserver on UNIX hosts instead of having
to use killall to stop the process and a script to start it when
configurations are changed or virtual domains added or removed.

* The FTP server still won't handle hardly any load at all - I've found I
can't use it for serious FTP work.

* The webbased admin panel still positively rocks - much easier than editing
Apache's config file via ssh, and then reloading the server with
/etc/init.d/apache reload.  But I can't get Xitami's server restart function
to work every time when throwing in a new domain or making other config
changes that require reload of the /usr/local/bin/xitami/defaults.cfg file.
I've found I still have to ssh to the box, kill xitami, then execute the
start script to fire it back up and force the config file reload.  Others
have this problem?

Regards,
--
Chris Olson
System Administrator
AST Communications  http://www.astcomm.net
